## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - query.FieldContext
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_1552071599.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. query.FieldContext

# query.FieldContext

Note: 

JavaScript does not include an enumeration type. The SuiteScript 2.x documentation uses the term enumeration (or enum) to describe a plain JavaScript object with a flat, map-like structure. In this object, each key points to a read-only string value.

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Enum Description** | Holds the string values for the field context to use when creating a column using [Query.createColumn(options)](section_1510780373.html) or [Component.createColumn(options)](section_1510784945.html).  The field context determines how field values are displayed in a column. For example, you can specify that a column should display raw data (such as internal IDs), consolidated or converted amounts (such as currency totals), or user-friendly values (such as names). |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Sibling Module Members** | [N/query Module Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510352106) |
| **Since** | 2019.1 |

## Values

| Value | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `CONVERTED` | Displays converted currency amounts using the exchange rate that was in effect on a specific date. |
| `CURRENCY_CONSOLIDATED` | Displays consolidated currency amounts in the base currency. |
| `DISPLAY` | Displays user-friendly field values. For example, for the entity field on Transaction records, using the `DISPLAY` enum value displays the name of the entity instead of its ID. |
| `HIERARCHY` | Displays user-friendly field values for hierarchical fields (for example, 'Parent Company : SUB CAD'). This value is similar to the `DISPLAY` enum value but applies to hierarchical fields. |
| `HIERARCHY_IDENTIFIER` | Displays raw field values for hierarchical fields (for example, '1 : 5'). This value is similar to the `RAW` enum value but applies to hierarchical fields. |
| `RAW` | Displays raw field values. For example, for the entity field on Transaction records, using the `RAW` enum value displays the ID of the entity. |
| `SIGN_CONSOLIDATED` | - |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myTransactionQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.TRANSACTION
    });
    var myContextColumn = myTransactionQuery.createColumn({
        fieldId: 'netamount',
        context: query.FieldContext.CURRENCY_CONSOLIDATED
    });
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - Query.join(options)
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_1510275377.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. [query.Query](section_1510275177.html)
7. Query.join(options)

# Query.join(options)

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Method Description** | Creates a join relationship.  Important:  This method is an alias to [Query.autoJoin(options)](section_1530819144.html). Use [Query.autoJoin(options)](section_1530819144.html) instead of this method to create simple joins. Use [Query.joinFrom(options)](section_1530819218.html) and [Query.joinTo(options)](section_1530819329.html) to create explicit directional joins.  Use the method [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html) to create your initial query definition ([query.Query](section_1510275177.html)). The initial query definition uses one query type. For available query types, see [query.Type](section_1510878994.html).  After you create the initial query definition, use `Query.join(options)` to create your first join ([query.Component](section_1510779141.html)). Then use [Component.autoJoin(options)](section_1530818573.html) to create each subsequent join ([query.Component](section_1510779141.html)).  Note:  This method is a shortcut for the chained [Query.root](section_1510781874.html) and [Component.join(options)](section_1510784833.html): `Query.root.join(options)`. The [Query.root](section_1510781874.html) property references the root component, which is a [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) object.  Important:  The N/query module supports the same record types that are supported by the SuiteAnalytics Workbook interface. For more information, see [Available Record Types](section_1543418356.html). |
| **Returns** | [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Governance** | None |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) |
| **Sibling Object Members** | [Query Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510352143) |
| **Since** | 2018.1 |

## Parameters

Note: 

The `options` parameter is a JavaScript object.

| Parameter | Type | Required / Optional | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `options.fieldId` | string | required | The column type (field type) that joins the parent component to the new component. This value determines the columns on which the components are joined and the type of the newly joined component.  Obtain this value from the Records Catalog. The Records Catalog lists every record type and field that is available using SuiteAnalytics Workbook and the N/query module. For more information, see [Records Catalog Overview](article_159367781370.html). |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myTransactionQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.TRANSACTION
    });
    var myEntityJoin = myTransactionQuery.join({
        fieldId: 'entity'
    });
    myTransactionQuery.columns = [
        myEntityJoin.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'subsidiary'
        })
    ];
    myTransactionQuery.sort = [
        myTransactionQuery.createSort({
            column: myTransactionQuery.columns[0],
            ascending: false
        })
    ];
    var results = myTransactionQuery.runPaged({
        pageSize: 10
    });
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - Query.joinFrom(options)
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_1530819218.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. [query.Query](section_1510275177.html)
7. Query.joinFrom(options)

# Query.joinFrom(options)

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Method Description** | Creates an explicit directional join relationship from a child component to its parent component (an inverse join). This method sets the [Component.source](section_1510785292.html) property on the returned [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) object.  Use the method [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html) to create your initial query definition ([query.Query](section_1510275177.html)). The initial query definition uses one query type. For available query types, see [query.Type](section_1510878994.html).  After you create the initial query definition, use this method to create your first join as an explicit directional join from another component to this component.  Note:  This method is a shortcut for the chained [Query.root](section_1510781874.html) and [Component.joinFrom(options)](section_1530818705.html): `Query.root.joinFrom(options)`. The [Query.root](section_1510781874.html) property references the root component, which is a [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) object.  Important:  The N/query module supports the same record types that are supported by the SuiteAnalytics Workbook interface. For more information, see [Available Record Types](section_1543418356.html). |
| **Returns** | [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Governance** | None |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) |
| **Sibling Object Members** | [Query Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510352143) |
| **Since** | 2018.2 |

## Parameters

Note: 

The `options` parameter is a JavaScript object.

| Parameter | Type | Required / Optional | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `options.fieldId` | string | required | The column type (field type) that joins the parent component to the new component.  Obtain this value from the Records Catalog. The Records Catalog lists every record type and field that is available using SuiteAnalytics Workbook and the N/query module. For more information, see [Records Catalog Overview](article_159367781370.html). |
| `options.source` | string | required | The query type of the component joined to this component. This value sets the [Component.source](section_1510785292.html) property.  This value can be described as the inverse relationship of this component, and it determines the source query type of the newly joined component. |

## Errors

| Error Code | Thrown If |
| --- | --- |
| `RELATIONSHIP_ALREADY_USED` | The specified join relationship already exists. |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myEmployeeQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.EMPLOYEE
    });
    var myTransactionJoin = myEmployeeQuery.joinFrom({
        fieldId: 'entity',
        source: 'transaction'
    });
    myEmployeeQuery.columns = [
        myEmployeeQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'entityid'
        }),
        myTransactionJoin.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'entity'
        }),
        myTransactionJoin.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'daysoverduesearch'
        })
    ];
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - Query.joinTo(options)
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_1530819329.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. [query.Query](section_1510275177.html)
7. Query.joinTo(options)

# Query.joinTo(options)

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Method Description** | Creates an explicit directional join relationship from a parent component to its child component (a forward join). This method sets the [Component.target](section_1510785266.html) property on the returned [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) object.  Use the method [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html) to create your initial query definition ([query.Query](section_1510275177.html)). The initial query definition uses one query type. For available query types, see [query.Type](section_1510878994.html).  After you create the initial query definition, use this method to create your first join as an explicit directional join to another component from this component.  Note:  This method is a shortcut for the chained [Query.root](section_1510781874.html) and [Component.joinTo(options)](section_1530818855.html): `Query.root.autoJoin(options)`. The [Query.root](section_1510781874.html) property references the root component, which is a [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) object.  Important:  The N/query module supports the same record types that are supported by the SuiteAnalytics Workbook interface. For more information, see [Available Record Types](section_1543418356.html). |
| **Returns** | [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Governance** | None |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) |
| **Sibling Object Members** | [Query Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510352143) |
| **Since** | 2018.2 |

## Parameters

Note: 

The `options` parameter is a JavaScript object.

| Parameter | Type | Required / Optional | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `options.fieldId` | string | required | The column type (field type) that joins the parent component to the new component.  Obtain this value from the Records Catalog. The Records Catalog lists every record type and field that is available using SuiteAnalytics Workbook and the N/query module. For more information, see [Records Catalog Overview](article_159367781370.html). |
| `options.target` | string | required | The query type of the component joined to this component. This value sets the [Component.target](section_1510785266.html) property.  This value can be described as the relationship of this component, and it determines the target query type of the newly joined component. |

## Errors

| Error Code | Thrown If |
| --- | --- |
| `RELATIONSHIP_ALREADY_USED` | The specified join relationship already exists. |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myTransactionQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.TRANSACTION
    });
    var myEmployeeJoin = myTransactionQuery.joinTo({
        fieldId: 'createdby',
        target: 'employee'
    });
    myTransactionQuery.columns = [
        myTransactionQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'entity'
        }),
        myEmployeeJoin.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'entityid'
        }),
        myEmployeeJoin.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'email'
        })
    ];
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - query.load(options)
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_1510349101.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. query.load(options)

# query.load(options)

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Method Description** | Loads an existing query as a [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) object.  Use this method to load a query definition that was previously created using the SuiteAnalytics Workbook UI. After the query is loaded, you can modify the query definition (for example, by setting additional property values), join the query definition with other query types, and perform the query in the same way as queries that you create using [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html).  You can provide either the workbook ID or the dataset ID of the query definition to load. You can obtain these IDs in the SuiteAnalytics Workbook UI. For more information, see [Navigating SuiteAnalytics Workbook](chapter_1544220943.html).  This method loads only the table view in the specified workbook. However, a workbook can include no table views, or it can include multiple table views. This method throws an exception in each of these cases (see [Errors](#subsect_1531761778)). If a workbook includes multiple table views, you can use [query.listTables(options)](section_158289760700.html) to determine the ID of a specific table view. You can use this ID to load the corresponding table view.  Important:  The N/query module lets you create and run queries using the SuiteAnalytics Workbook query process. You can use the N/query module to load and delete existing queries, but you cannot save queries. You can save queries using the SuiteAnalytics Workbook interface. For more information, see [Navigating SuiteAnalytics Workbook](chapter_1544220943.html). |
| **Returns** | [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Governance** | 5 units |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Sibling Module Members** | [N/query Module Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510352106) |
| **Since** | 2018.2 |

## Parameters

Note: 

The `options` parameter is a JavaScript object.

| Parameter | Type | Required / Optional | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `options.id` | string | required | The workbook ID or dataset ID of the query definition to load.  You can obtain these IDs in the SuiteAnalytics Workbook UI. For more information, see [Navigating SuiteAnalytics Workbook](chapter_1544220943.html). |

## Errors

| Error Code | Thrown If |
| --- | --- |
| `UNABLE_TO_LOAD_QUERY` | A query with the specified ID cannot be loaded because the query does not exist or you do not have permission to load it. |
| `WORKBOOK_MORE_TABLEVIEWS_ARE_ASSIGNED` | More than one table view is included in the specified workbook or dataset. |
| `WORKBOOK_NO_TABLEVIEW_IS_ASSIGNED` | No table views are included in the specified workbook or dataset. |

Note: 

If the loaded query does not return a desired sorting order, you must use the [Query.runPaged(options)](section_1510780277.html) method for default sorting or specify your custom sorting before script .

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myLoadedQuery = query.load({
        id: 'custworkbook237'
    });
    var mySalesRepJoin = myLoadedQuery.autoJoin({
        fieldId: 'salesrep'
    });
    var results = myLoadedQuery.run();
...
// Add additional code
```

* [SuiteScript 2.x](article_8161516336.html)

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - query.load.promise(options)

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)

# query.load.promise(options)

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Method Description** | Loads an existing query asynchronously as a [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) object.  Use this method to asynchronously load a query definition that was previously created using the SuiteAnalytics Workbook UI. After the query is loaded, you can modify the query definition (for example, by setting additional property values), join the query definition with other query types, and perform the query in the same way as queries that you create using [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html).  You can provide either the workbook ID or the dataset ID of the query definition to load. You can obtain these IDs in the SuiteAnalytics Workbook UI. For more information, see [Navigating SuiteAnalytics Workbook](chapter_1544220943.html).  This method loads only the table view in the specified workbook. However, a workbook can include no table views, or it can include multiple table views. This method throws an exception in each of these cases (see [Errors](section_1510349101.html#subsect_1531761778)). If a workbook includes multiple table views, you can use [query.listTables(options)](section_158289760700.html) to determine the ID of a specific table view. You can use this ID to load the corresponding table view.  Important:  The N/query module lets you create and run queries using the SuiteAnalytics Workbook query process. You can use the N/query module to load and delete existing queries, but you cannot save queries. You can save queries using the SuiteAnalytics Workbook interface. For more information, see [Navigating SuiteAnalytics Workbook](chapter_1544220943.html).  Note:  The parameters and errors thrown for this method are the same as those for [query.load(options)](section_1510349101.html). For more information about promises, see [Promise Object](section_4387812940.html). |
| **Returns** | [Promise Object](section_4387812940.html) |
| **Synchronous Version** | [query.load(options)](section_1510349101.html) |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Governance** | 5 units |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Sibling Module Members** | [N/query Module Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510352106) |
| **Since** | 2018.2 |

## Parameters

Note: 

The `options` parameter is a JavaScript object.

| Parameter | Type | Required / Optional | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `options.id` | string | required | The workbook ID or dataset ID of the query definition to load.  You can obtain these IDs in the SuiteAnalytics Workbook UI. For more information, see [Navigating SuiteAnalytics Workbook](chapter_1544220943.html). |

## Errors

| Error Code | Thrown If |
| --- | --- |
| `UNABLE_TO_LOAD_QUERY` | A query with the specified ID cannot be loaded because the query does not exist or you do not have permission to load it. |
| `WORKBOOK_MORE_TABLEVIEWS_ARE_ASSIGNED` | More than one table view is included in the specified workbook or dataset. |
| `WORKBOOK_NO_TABLEVIEW_IS_ASSIGNED` | No table views are included in the specified workbook or dataset. |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete promise script example, see [Promise Object](section_4387812940.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myLoadedQuery = query.load.promise({
        id: 'custworkbook237'
    }).then (function(result) {
        // Process the result
    });
    var mySalesRepJoin = myLoadedQuery.autoJoin({
        fieldId: 'salesrep'
    });
    var results = myLoadedQuery.run();
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - Query.not(condition)
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_1510780462.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. [query.Query](section_1510275177.html)
7. Query.not(condition)

# Query.not(condition)

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Method Description** | Creates a new condition (a [query.Condition](section_1510779210.html) object) that corresponds to a logical negation (NOT) of the argument passed to the method. The argument must be a [query.Condition](section_1510779210.html) object.  A condition narrows the query results. The [query.Condition](section_1510779210.html) object acts in the same capacity as the [search.Filter](section_4345767603.html) object in the [N/search Module](section_4345764122.html). The primary difference is that [query.Condition](section_1510779210.html) objects can contain other [query.Condition](section_1510779210.html) objects.  To create conditions:   * Use [Query.createCondition(options)](section_1510780329.html) to create conditions for the initial query definition created with [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html). * Use [Component.createCondition(options)](section_1510784922.html) to create conditions for the join relationships created with [Query.autoJoin(options)](section_1530819144.html) and [Component.autoJoin(options)](section_1530818573.html). * If you have multiple conditions, use them to create a new parent condition with the methods [Query.and(conditions)](section_1510780422.html), [Query.or(conditions)](section_1510780444.html), and `Query.not()`. * Assign your parent condition to [Query.condition](section_1510781832.html). For an example, see [Syntax](#subsect_1530622328). |
| **Returns** | [query.Condition](section_1510779210.html) |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Governance** | None |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) |
| **Sibling Object Members** | [Query Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510352143) |
| **Since** | 2018.1 |

## Parameters

| Parameter | Type | Required / Optional | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `condition` | [query.Condition](section_1510779210.html) | required | One condition object. |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myCustomerQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.CUSTOMER
    });
    var mySalesRepJoin = myCustomerQuery.autoJoin({
        fieldId: 'salesrep'
    });
    var myLocationJoin = mySalesRepJoin.autoJoin({
        fieldId: 'location'
    });
    var firstCondition = myCustomerQuery.createCondition({
        fieldId: 'id',
        operator: query.Operator.EQUAL,
        values: 107
    });
    var secondCondition = myCustomerQuery.createCondition({
        fieldId: 'id',
        operator: query.Operator.EQUAL,
        values: 2647
    });
    var thirdCondition = mySalesRepJoin.createCondition({
        fieldId: 'email',
        operator: query.Operator.START_WITH_NOT,
        values: 'foo'
    });
    myCustomerQuery.condition = myCustomerQuery.and(thirdCondition, myCustomerQuery.not( myCustomerQuery.or(firstCondition, secondCondition)));
    var resultSet = myCustomerQuery.run();
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - query.Operator
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_1510275752.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. query.Operator

# query.Operator

Note: 

JavaScript does not include an enumeration type. The SuiteScript 2.x documentation uses the term enumeration (or enum) to describe a plain JavaScript object with a flat, map-like structure. In this object, each key points to a read-only string value.

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Enum Description** | Holds the string values for operators supported in SuiteScript Analytic APIs.  SuiteScript Analytic APIs help you work with analytical data in NetSuite using SuiteScript. For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Analytic APIs](article_159524581218.html).  This enum is used to specify the operator argument to [Query.createCondition(options)](section_1510780329.html) and [Component.createCondition(options)](section_1510784922.html). This enum is also used to specify the operator argument to methods in the N/dataset and N/workbook modules, such as [dataset.createCondition(options)](section_158990217350.html) and [workbook.createTableColumnFilter(options)](section_159051973321.html). For more information, see [Workbook API](article_159414531069.html).  Values for this enum are listed in the [Values](#subsect_1510778814) section. The following columns provide information about each operator:   * **Value** - Use these values to specify operators in most queries (for example, `query.Operator.BEFORE`). To use these values, you must include the N/query module in your script. * **Mapped String Value** - Use these values as strings that represent the corresponding operators (for example, `'BEFORE'`). To use these values, you do not need to include the N/query module in your script. * **Use For** - Use this column to determine the value types that each operator supports. For example, the `query.Operator.AFTER` operator is designed to be used with date/time values, and you cannot use this operator with string or values. Some operators are similar but are designed to be used with different value types (such as `query.Operator.IS` for values and `query.Operator.EQUAL` for numeric values).   For multi-select fields, you can use the `query.Operator.INCLUDE_*` and `query.Operator.EXCLUDE_*` values to specify a set of exact field values. For example, to obtain script deployment records that apply to all contexts except the `WEBAPP` and `WEBSTORE` contexts, you can use the `query.Operator.EXCLUDE_ALL` operator. You cannot use the `query.Operator.ANY_OF_NOT` operator to obtain these records, because this operator uses an implicit OR operator between all specified values. The `query.Operator.EXCLUDE_ALL` operator uses an implicit AND operator between all specified values, which lets you create more complex conditions. |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Sibling Module Members** | [N/query Module Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510352106) |
| **Since** | 2018.1 |

## Values

| Value | Mapped String Value | Use For |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `AFTER` | AFTER | Date/time values |
| `AFTER_NOT` | AFTER\_NOT | Date/time values |
| `ANY_OF` | ANY\_OF | Single-select fields  Multi-select fields |
| `ANY_OF_NOT` | ANY\_OF\_NOT | Single-select fields  Multi-select fields |
| `BEFORE` | BEFORE | Date/time values |
| `BEFORE_NOT` | BEFORE\_NOT | Date/time values |
| `BETWEEN` | BETWEEN | Numbers |
| `BETWEEN_NOT` | BETWEEN\_NOT | Numbers |
| `CONTAIN` | CONTAIN | Strings |
| `CONTAIN_NOT` | CONTAIN\_NOT | Strings |
| `EMPTY` | EMPTY | Single-select fields  Multi-select fields |
| `EMPTY_NOT` | EMPTY\_NOT | Single-select fields  Multi-select fields |
| `ENDWITH` | ENDWITH | Strings |
| `ENDWITH_NOT` | ENDWITH\_NOT | Strings |
| `EQUAL` | EQUAL | Numbers |
| `EQUAL_NOT` | EQUAL\_NOT | Numbers |
| `EXCLUDE_ALL` | MN\_EXCLUDE | Multi-select fields |
| `EXCLUDE_ANY` | MN\_EXCLUDE\_ALL | Multi-select fields |
| `EXCLUDE_EXACTLY` | MN\_EXCLUDE\_EXACTLY | Multi-select fields |
| `GREATER` | GREATER | Numbers |
| `GREATER_NOT` | GREATER\_NOT | Numbers |
| `GREATER_OR_EQUAL` | GREATER\_OR\_EQUAL | Numbers |
| `GREATER_OR_EQUAL_NOT` | GREATER\_OR\_EQUAL\_NOT | Numbers |
| `INCLUDE_ALL` | MN\_INCLUDE\_ALL | Multi-select fields |
| `INCLUDE_ANY` | MN\_INCLUDE | Multi-select fields |
| `INCLUDE_EXACTLY` | MN\_INCLUDE\_EXACTLY | Multi-select fields |
| `IS` | IS | values |
| `IS_NOT` | IS\_NOT | values |
| `LESS` | LESS | Numbers |
| `LESS_NOT` | LESS\_NOT | Numbers |
| `LESS_OR_EQUAL` | LESS\_OR\_EQUAL | Numbers |
| `LESS_OR_EQUAL_NOT` | LESS\_OR\_EQUAL\_NOT | Numbers |
| `ON` | ON | Date/time values |
| `ON_NOT` | ON\_NOT | Date/time values |
| `ON_OR_AFTER` | ON\_OR\_AFTER | Date/time values |
| `ON_OR_AFTER_NOT` | ON\_OR\_AFTER\_NOT | Date/time values |
| `ON_OR_BEFORE` | ON\_OR\_BEFORE | Date/time values |
| `ON_OR_BEFORE_NOT` | ON\_OR\_BEFORE\_NOT | Date/time values |
| `START_WITH` | START\_WITH | Strings |
| `START_WITH_NOT` | START\_WITH\_NOT | Strings |
| `WITHIN` | WITHIN | Date/time values |
| `WITHIN_NOT` | WITHIN\_NOT | Date/time values |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myCustomerQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.CUSTOMER
    });
    var mySalesRepJoin = myCustomerQuery.autoJoin({
        fieldId: 'salesrep'
    });
    var firstCondition = myCustomerQuery.createCondition({
        fieldId: 'id',
        operator: query.Operator.EQUAL,
        values: 107
    });
    var secondCondition = myCustomerQuery.createCondition({
        fieldId: 'id',
        operator: query.Operator.EQUAL,
        values: 2647
    });
    var thirdCondition = mySalesRepJoin.createCondition({
        fieldId: 'email',
        operator: query.Operator.START_WITH_NOT,
        values: 'foo'
    });
    myCustomerQuery.condition = myCustomerQuery.and(thirdCondition, myCustomerQuery.not( myCustomerQuery.or(firstCondition, secondCondition)));
    var resultSet = myCustomerQuery.run();
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - Query.or(conditions)
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_1510780444.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. [query.Query](section_1510275177.html)
7. Query.or(conditions)

# Query.or(conditions)

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Method Description** | Creates a new condition (a [query.Condition](section_1510779210.html) object) that corresponds to a logical disjunction (OR) of the arguments passed to the method. The arguments must be one or more [query.Condition](section_1510779210.html) objects.  A condition narrows the query results. The [query.Condition](section_1510779210.html) object acts in the same capacity as the [search.Filter](section_4345767603.html) object in the [N/search Module](section_4345764122.html). The primary difference is that [query.Condition](section_1510779210.html) objects can contain other [query.Condition](section_1510779210.html) objects.  To create conditions:   * Use [Query.createCondition(options)](section_1510780329.html) to create conditions for the initial query definition created with [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html). * Use [Component.createCondition(options)](section_1510784922.html) to create conditions for the join relationships created with [Query.autoJoin(options)](section_1530819144.html) and [Component.autoJoin(options)](section_1530818573.html). * If you have multiple conditions, use them to create a new parent condition with the methods [Query.and(conditions)](section_1510780422.html), `Query.or()`, and [Query.not(condition)](section_1510780462.html). * Assign your parent condition to [Query.condition](section_1510781832.html). For an example, see [Syntax](#subsect_1530622396). |
| **Returns** | [query.Condition](section_1510779210.html) |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Governance** | None |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) |
| **Sibling Object Members** | [Query Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510352143) |
| **Since** | 2018.1 |

## Parameters

| Parameter | Type | Required / Optional | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `condition` 1 - n | [query.Condition](section_1510779210.html)[] | required | One or more condition objects.  There is no limit on the number of conditions you can specify. |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myCustomerQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.CUSTOMER
    });
    var mySalesRepJoin = myCustomerQuery.autoJoin({
        fieldId: 'salesrep'
    });
    var myLocationJoin = mySalesRepJoin.autoJoin({
        fieldId: 'location'
    });
    var firstCondition = myCustomerQuery.createCondition({
        fieldId: 'id',
        operator: query.Operator.EQUAL,
        values: 107
    });
    var secondCondition = myCustomerQuery.createCondition({
        fieldId: 'id',
        operator: query.Operator.EQUAL,
        values: 2647
    });
    var thirdCondition = mySalesRepJoin.createCondition({
        fieldId: 'email',
        operator: query.Operator.START_WITH_NOT,
        values: 'foo'
    });
    myCustomerQuery.condition = myCustomerQuery.and(thirdCondition, myCustomerQuery.not(myCustomerQuery.or(firstCondition, secondCondition)));
    var resultSet = myCustomerQuery.run();
...
// Add additional code
```

```
...

    type: query.Type.CUSTOMER
    });

            fieldId: 'entityid'
        }),
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'firstname'
        }),
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'email'
        })
    ];
    var myPagedResults = myCustomerQuery.runPaged({
        pageSize: 10
    })

    // Fetch results using an iterator
    var iterator = myPagedResults.iterator();
    iterator.each(function(resultPage) {
        var currentPage = resultPage.value;
        log.debug(currentPage.pageRange.size);
        return true;
    });

    // Alternatively, fetch results using a loop
    for (var i = 0; i < myPagedResults.pageRanges.length; i++) {
        var currentPage = myPagedResults.fetch(i); log.debug(currentPage.pageRange.size);
    }
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - query.PagedData
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_1510779273.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. query.PagedData

# query.PagedData

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Object Description** | A set of paged query results. This object also contains information about the set of paged results it encapsulates.  Use [Query.runPaged(options)](section_1510780277.html) or [Query.runPaged.promise(options)](section_1510780308.html) to create this object.  For paged queries, the maximum number of result rows per page is 1000. The minimum number of result rows per page is 5, except for the last page in the result set (because the last page may include fewer than 5 results). |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Methods and Properties** | [PagedData Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510860746) |
| **Since** | 2018.1 |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myCustomerQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.CUSTOMER
    });
    myCustomerQuery.columns = [
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'entityid'
        }),
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'firstname'
        }),
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'email'
        })
    ];
    var myPagedResults = myCustomerQuery.runPaged({
        pageSize: 10
    });

    // Fetch results using an iterator
    var iterator = myPagedResults.iterator();
    iterator.each(function(resultPage) {
        var currentPage = resultPage.value;
        var currentPagedData = currentPage.pagedData;
        log.debug(currentPage.pageRange.size);
        return true;
    });

    // Alternatively, fetch results using a loop
    for (var i = 0; i < myPagedResults.pageRanges.length; i++) {
        var currentPage = myPagedResults.fetch(i);
        var currentPagedData = currentPage.pagedData;
        log.debug(currentPage.pageRange.size);
    }
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - query.Query
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_1510275177.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. query.Query

# query.Query

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Object Description** | The `query.Query` object encapsulates the query definition. To create a query with the N/query module:   1. Use the [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html) method to create your query definition (this object). The initial query definition uses one query type. For available query types, see [query.Type](section_1510878994.html). 2. After you create the initial query definition, use [Query.autoJoin(options)](section_1530819144.html) to create your first join. 3. Then use either [Query.autoJoin(options)](section_1530819144.html) or [Component.autoJoin(options)](section_1530818573.html) to create subsequent joins.   The query definition always contains at least one [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) object. The [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) object encapsulates one component of the query definition. Each new component is created as a child to the previous component, and all components exist as children to the query definition.  You can think of a component as a building block; each new component builds on the previous component created. The last component created encapsulates the relationship between it and all of its parent components.  Queries with joins contain multiple components. The query definition contains a child [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) object for each of the following:   * **The initial query definition:** The initial [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) object is called the root component. It encapsulates the initial query type passed to [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html). The root component is automatically created with the initial query definition and is a child to the `query.Query` object. The [Query.root](section_1510781874.html) property contains a reference to the root component. * **The first join:** The second [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) object is created with [Query.autoJoin(options)](section_1530819144.html). It encapsulates the relationship between the initial query definition and the second query type. This relationship is determined by the field ID passed to [Query.autoJoin(options)](section_1530819144.html). The second [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) object is a child to the root component. * **Each subsequent join:** The third [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) object is created with [Query.autoJoin(options)](section_1530819144.html) or [Component.autoJoin(options)](section_1530818573.html). All subsequent joins are also created with [Query.autoJoin(options)](section_1530819144.html) or [Component.autoJoin(options)](section_1530818573.html). Each of these [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) objects encapsulates the relationship between all previous query types and the new query type. This relationship is determined by the field ID passed to [Component.autoJoin(options)](section_1530818573.html). |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Methods and Properties** | [Query Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510352143) |
| **Since** | 2018.1 |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myTransactionQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.TRANSACTION
    });
    var myEntityJoin = myTransactionQuery.autoJoin({
        fieldId: 'entity'
    });
    myTransactionQuery.columns = [
        myEntityJoin.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'subsidiary'
        })
    ];
    myTransactionQuery.sort = [
        myTransactionQuery.createSort({
            column: myTransactionQuery.columns[0],
            ascending: false
        })
    ];
    var results = myTransactionQuery.runPaged({
        pageSize: 10
    });
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - query.RelativeDate
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_1544109440.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. query.RelativeDate

# query.RelativeDate

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Object Description** | A relative date to use in query conditions.  Use [query.createRelativeDate(options)](section_1544108154.html) to create this object. After you create this object, you can use it in the `values` parameter of [Query.createCondition(options)](section_1510780329.html) or [Component.createCondition(options)](section_1510784922.html).  This object represents a specific moment in time, and you can use it to create query conditions using operators from the [query.Operator](section_1510275752.html) enum, such as `query.Operator.AFTER`, `query.Operator.BEFORE`, and `query.Operator.WITHIN`. For more information about relative dates, see [Relative Dates in the N/query Module](section_1549916938.html). |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Methods and Properties** | [RelativeDate Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1544530447) |
| **Since** | 2019.1 |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myEndDate = query.createRelativeDate({
        dateId: query.DateId.WEEKS_AGO,
        value: 2
    });
    var myComplexCondition = myQuery.createCondition({
        fieldId: 'trandate',
        operator: query.Operator.WITHIN,
        values: [query.RelativeDateRange.THREE_FISCAL_YEARS_AGO.start, myEndDate]
    });
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - query.RelativeDateRange
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_1544111773.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. query.RelativeDateRange

# query.RelativeDateRange

Note: 

JavaScript does not include an enumeration type. The SuiteScript 2.x documentation uses the term enumeration (or enum) to describe a plain JavaScript object with a flat, map-like structure. In this object, each key points to a read-only string value.

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Enum Description** | Holds [query.RelativeDate](section_1544109440.html) object values for supported date ranges in relative dates.  This enum is used to pass the values argument to [Query.createCondition(options)](section_1510780329.html) and [Component.createCondition(options)](section_1510784922.html). It is also used as the value of the [RelativeDate.value](section_1544109837.html) property. Each value in this enum represents a date range. When [Query.createCondition(options)](section_1510780329.html) or [Component.createCondition(options)](section_1510784922.html) is called with a [query.RelativeDate](section_1544109440.html) object as the `values` argument, this object is set as the value of the [RelativeDate.value](section_1544109837.html) property.  When creating a condition using [Query.createCondition(options)](section_1510780329.html) or [Component.createCondition(options)](section_1510784922.html), use the values in this enum (along with values in the [query.Operator](section_1510275752.html) enum) to specify a range of dates relative to the current date. For example, to create a condition to match dates that occur before the current date, use the `query.RelativeDateRange.TODAY` enum value and the `query.Operator.BEFORE` enum value. To create a condition to match dates that occur after last year, use the `query.RelativeDateRange.LAST_YEAR` enum value and the `query.Operator.AFTER` enum value. For more information about relative dates, see [Relative Dates in the N/query Module](section_1549916938.html).  The values in this enum might look similar to the values in the [query.DateId](section_1544111587.html) enum, but each enum is used for a different purpose:   * Use [query.DateId](section_1544111587.html) enum values to create a [query.RelativeDate](section_1544109440.html) object using [query.createRelativeDate(options)](section_1544108154.html). After you create this object, you can use it in query conditions that you create using [Query.createCondition(options)](section_1510780329.html) or [Component.createCondition(options)](section_1510784922.html). * Use `query.RelativeDateRange` enum values directly in query conditions that you create using [Query.createCondition(options)](section_1510780329.html) or [Component.createCondition(options)](section_1510784922.html). Each value in the `query.RelativeDateRange` enum represents a date range, and you can use these values in the `values` parameter of [Query.createCondition(options)](section_1510780329.html) or [Component.createCondition(options)](section_1510784922.html). |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Sibling Module Members** | [N/query Module Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510352106) |
| **Since** | 2019.1 |

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - query.Result

# query.Result

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Object Description** | A single row of the result set ([query.ResultSet](section_1510779235.html)). |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Methods and Properties** | [Result Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510858930) |
| **Since** | 2018.1 |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myCustomerQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.CUSTOMER
    });
    myCustomerQuery.columns = [
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'entityid'
        }),
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'firstname'
        }),
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'email'
        })
    ];
    var queryResultSet = myCustomerQuery.run();
    
    // Fetch results using an iterator
    var iterator = queryResultSet.iterator();
    iterator.each(function(result) {
        var currentResult = result.value;
        log.debug(currentResult);
        return true;
    });

    // Alternatively, fetch results using a loop
    var queryResults = queryResultSet.results;
    for (var i = 0; i < queryResults.length; i++) {
        var currentResult = queryResults[i];
        log.debug(currentResult);
    }
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - query.ResultSet
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_1510779235.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. query.ResultSet

# query.ResultSet

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Object Description** | The set of results returned by the query. Use [Query.run(options)](section_1510780212.html) or [Query.run.promise()](section_1510780250.html) to create this object.  The maximum number of results in a `ResultSet` object is 5000. If a query matches more than 5000 results, you must use [Query.runPaged(options)](section_1510780277.html) or [Query.runPaged.promise(options)](section_1510780308.html) to retrieve the full set of results. |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Methods and Properties** | [ResultSet Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510790719) |
| **Since** | 2018.1 |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myCustomerQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.CUSTOMER
    });
    myCustomerQuery.columns = [
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'entityid'
        }),
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'email'
        })
    ];
    var resultSet = myCustomerQuery.run();
    var results = resultSet.results;
    for (var i = results.length - 1; i >= 0; i--)
        log.debug(results[i].values);
...
// Add additional code
```

# query.ReturnType

Note: 

JavaScript does not include an enumeration type. The SuiteScript 2.x documentation uses the term enumeration (or enum) to describe a plain JavaScript object with a flat, map-like structure. In this object, each key points to a read-only string value.

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Enum Description** | Holds the string values for the formula return types supported with the [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html).  This enum is used to pass the formula return type argument to [Query.createColumn(options)](section_1510780373.html), [Component.createColumn(options)](section_1510784945.html), [Query.createCondition(options)](section_1510780329.html), and [Component.createCondition(options)](section_1510784922.html).  For more information about these return types, see [Formula Fields](section_1544128605.html).  For more information about formulas, see [SuiteAnalytics Workbook Overview](chapter_1503949328.html), [SQL Expressions](section_N2833020.html), and [Search Formula Examples and Tips](section_N662868.html). |

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - Query.root
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_1510781874.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. [query.Query](section_1510275177.html)
7. Query.root

# Query.root

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Property Description** | The root component of the query definition.  The initial [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) object is called the root component. It encapsulates the initial query type passed to [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html). The root component is automatically created with the [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) object and is a child of the [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) object. |
| **Type** | [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) (read-only) |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) |
| **Sibling Object Members** | [Query Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510352143) |
| **Since** | 2018.1 |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myCustomerQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.CUSTOMER
    });
    var theRoot = myCustomerQuery.root;
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - Query.run(options)
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_1510780212.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. [query.Query](section_1510275177.html)
7. Query.run(options)

# Query.run(options)

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Method Description** | Executes the query and returns the query result set.  This method returns a maximum of 5000 results in the query result set. If a query matches more than 5000 results, you must use [Query.runPaged(options)](section_1510780277.html) or [Query.runPaged.promise(options)](section_1510780308.html) to retrieve the full set of results. |
| **Returns** | [query.ResultSet](section_1510779235.html) |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Governance** | 10 units |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) |
| **Sibling Object Members** | [Query Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510352143) |
| **Since** | 2018.1 |

## Parameters

Note: 

The `options` parameter is a JavaScript object.

| Parameter | Type | Required / Optional | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `options.customScriptId` | string | optional | A unique identifier used for potential performance issues in a query.  If your query produces performance issues, the custom script ID identifies where the update will need to occur.  This ID can also be used as a precaution to speed up performance fixes, if necessary.  Note:  The Script ID must be unique or the performance enhancements will affect each query with the same customScriptID. |
| `options.metaDataProvider` | string | optional | Indicates whether the query should fail if you lack the necessary permissions for some fields or records.  If set to `SUITE_QL`:  The query fails if you attempt to access fields or records without the necessary permissions.  If set to `STATIC`:  The query succeeds even if you lack permissions for some fields or records, but it does not return any data for those fields or records.  Defaults to `SUITE_QL`. |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myCustomerQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.CUSTOMER
    });
    var mySalesRepJoin = myCustomerQuery.autoJoin({
        fieldId: 'salesrep'
    });
    myCustomerQuery.columns = [
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'entityid'
        }),
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'id'
        }),
        mySalesRepJoin.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'entityid'
        }),
        mySalesRepJoin.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'email'
        }),
        mySalesRepJoin.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'hiredate'
        })
    ];
    myCustomerQuery.sort = [
        myCustomerQuery.createSort({
            column: myCustomerQuery.columns[1]
        }),
        mySalesRepJoin.createSort({
            column: mySalesRepJoin.columns[0],
            ascending: false
        })
    ];
    var resultSet = myCustomerQuery.run({
        customScriptId: 'myCustomScriptId'
    });
...
// Add additional code
```

# Query.run.promise()

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Method Description** | Executes the query asynchronously and returns the query result set.  Note:  The parameters and errors thrown for this method are the same as those for [Query.run(options)](section_1510780212.html). For more information about promises, see [Promise Object](section_4387812940.html). |
| **Returns** | [Promise Object](section_4387812940.html) |
| **Synchronous Version** | [Query.run(options)](section_1510780212.html) |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Governance** | 10 units |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) |
| **Sibling Object Members** | [Query Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510352143) |
| **Since** | 2018.1 |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete promise script example, see [Promise Object](section_4387812940.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myCustomerQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.CUSTOMER
    });
    var mySalesRepJoin = myCustomerQuery.autoJoin({
        fieldId: 'salesrep'
    });
    myCustomerQuery.columns = [
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'entityid'
        }),
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'id'
        }),
        mySalesRepJoin.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'entityid'
        }),
        mySalesRepJoin.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'email'
        }),
        mySalesRepJoin.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'hiredate'
        })
    ];
    myCustomerQuery.sort = [
        myCustomerQuery.createSort({
            column: myCustomerQuery.columns[1]
        }),
        mySalesRepJoin.createSort({
            column: mySalesRepJoin.columns[0],
            ascending: false
        })
    ];
    var resultSet = myCustomerQuery.run.promise({
        customScriptId: 'myCustomScriptId'
    }).then (function(result) {
        // Process the result
    });
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - Query.runPaged(options)
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_1510780277.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. [query.Query](section_1510275177.html)
7. Query.runPaged(options)

# Query.runPaged(options)

Important: 

You must specify a sorting order in the query definition when using this method to avoid duplicate or missing results. The query definition must provide a unique and unambiguous sorting order with a specified precedence.

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Method Description** | Executes the query and returns a [query.PagedData](section_1510779273.html) object that represents the paged query results. You can iterate over this object to obtain each page of query results.  For paged queries, the maximum number of result rows per page is 1000. The minimum number of result rows per page is 5, except for the last page in the result set (because the last page may include fewer than 5 results). |
| **Returns** | [query.PagedData](section_1510779273.html) |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Governance** | 10 units |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) |
| **Sibling Object Members** | [Query Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510352143) |
| **Since** | 2018.1 |

## Parameters

Note: 

The `options` parameter is a JavaScript object.

| Parameter | Type | Required / Optional | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `options.pageSize` | string | optional | The size of each page in the query results.  The default page size is 50 results per page. |
| `options.customScriptId` | string | optional | A unique identifier used for potential performance issues in a query.  If your query produces performance issues, the custom script ID identifies where the update will need to occur.  This ID can also be used as a precaution to speed up performance fixes, if necessary.  Note:  The Script ID must be unique or the performance enhancements will affect each query with the same customScriptID. |
| `options.metaDataProvider` | string | optional | Indicates whether the query should fail if you lack the necessary permissions for some fields or records.  If set to `SUITE_QL`:  The query fails if you attempt to access fields or records without the necessary permissions.  If set to `STATIC`:  The query succeeds even if you lack permissions for some fields or records, but it does not return any data for those fields or records.  Defaults to `SUITE_QL`. |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myTransactionQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.TRANSACTION
    });
    var myEntityJoin = myTransactionQuery.autoJoin({
        fieldId: 'entity'
    });
    myTransactionQuery.columns = [
        myEntityJoin.createColumn({
            name: 'subsidiary'
        })
    ];
    myTransactionQuery.sort = [
        myTransactionQuery.createSort({
            column: myTransactionQuery.columns[0],
            ascending: false
        })
    ];
    var results = myTransactionQuery.runPaged({
        pageSize: 10,
        customScriptId: 'myCustomScriptId'
    });
    
    // Use the count property to count the search results easily
    var resultCount = myTransactionQuery.runPaged({
        pageSize: 10
    }).count;
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - query.runSuiteQL(options)
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_157960542026.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. query.runSuiteQL(options)

# query.runSuiteQL(options)

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Method Description** | Runs an arbitrary SuiteQL query.  SuiteQL is a query language based on the SQL-92 revision of the SQL database query language. It provides advanced query capabilities you can use to access your NetSuite records and data.  You can specify the SuiteQL query as one of the following:   * A string representation of the SuiteQL query     ```                           var results = query.runSuiteQL({       query: 'SELECT customer.entityid, customer.email FROM customer'   });   ``` * A [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html) object     ```                           // In this example, mySuiteQLCustomerQuery is an existing SuiteQL object   var results = query.runSuiteQL(mySuiteQLCustomerQuery);   ``` * A JavaScript Object that contains a `query` property and, optionally, a `params` property     ```                           var results = query.runSuiteQL({       query: 'SELECT customer.entityid, customer.email FROM customer WHERE customer.isperson = ?',       params: [true]   });   ```   Note:  This method can return a maximum of 5000 results. If you need to return more results, use [query.runSuiteQLPaged(options)](section_157960586441.html) instead.  For more information and examples of using SuiteQL in the N/query module, see [SuiteQL in the N/query Module](section_157960623712.html). For more information about SuiteQL in general, see [SuiteQL](section_156257770590.html). |
| **Returns** | [query.ResultSet](section_1510779235.html) |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Governance** | 10 units |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Sibling Module Members** | [N/query Module Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510352106) |
| **Since** | 2020.1 |

## Parameters

Note: 

The `options` parameter is a JavaScript object.

| Parameter | Type | Required / Optional | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `options.query` | string | required | The string representation of the SuiteQL query to run. |
| `options.params` | <string | number | > | optional | The parameters to use in the SuiteQL query. |
| `options.customScriptId` | string | optional | A unique identifier used for potential performance issues in a query.  If your query produces performance issues, the custom script ID identifies where the update will need to occur.  This ID can also be used as a precaution to speed up performance fixes, if necessary.  Note:  The Script ID must be unique or the performance enhancements will affect each query with the same customScriptID. |
| `options.metaDataProvider` | string | optional | Indicates whether the query should fail if you lack the necessary permissions for some fields or records.  If set to `SUITE_QL`:  The query fails if you attempt to access fields or records without the necessary permissions.  If set to `STATIC`:  The query succeeds even if you lack permissions for some fields or records, but it does not return any data for those fields or records.  Defaults to `SUITE_QL`. |

## Errors

| Error Code | Thrown If |
| --- | --- |
| `MISSING_REQD_ARGUMENT` | The parameter is missing. |
| `SSS_INVALID_TYPE_ARG` | Types other than string, number, or are included in the `options.params`. |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var results = query.runSuiteQL({
        query: 'SELECT customer.entityid, customer.email FROM customer WHERE customer.isperson = ?',
        params: [true],
        customScriptId: 'myCustomScriptId'
    });
...
// Add additional code
```

* [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
* [SuiteScript 2.x](article_8161516336.html)

# query.runSuiteQL.promise(options)

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Method Description** | Asynchronously runs an arbitrary SuiteQL query.  SuiteQL is a query language based on the SQL-92 revision of the SQL database query language. It provides advanced query capabilities you can use to access your NetSuite records and data.  You can specify the SuiteQL query as one of the following:   * A string representation of the SuiteQL query     ```                           var results = query.runSuiteQL.promise({       query: 'SELECT customer.entityid, customer.email FROM customer'   });   ``` * A [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html) object     ```                           // In this example, mySuiteQLCustomerQuery is an existing SuiteQL object   var results = query.runSuiteQL.promise(mySuiteQLCustomerQuery);   ``` * A JavaScript Object that contains a `query` property and, optionally, a `params` property     ```                           var results = query.runSuiteQL.promise({       query: 'SELECT customer.entityid, customer.email FROM customer WHERE customer.isperson = ?',       params: [true]   });   ```   Note:  This method can return a maximum of 5000 results. If you need to return more results, use [query.runSuiteQLPaged(options)](section_157960586441.html) instead.  For more information and examples of using SuiteQL in the N/query module, see [SuiteQL in the N/query Module](section_157960623712.html). For more information about SuiteQL in general, see [SuiteQL](section_156257770590.html). |
| **Returns** | [Promise Object](section_4387812940.html) |
| **Synchronous Version** | [query.runSuiteQL(options)](section_157960542026.html) |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Governance** | 10 units |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |

| --- | --- | --- | --- |

| `options.params` | <string | number | > | optional | The parameters to use in the SuiteQL query. |
| `options.customScriptId` | string | optional | A unique identifier used for potential performance issues in a query.  If your query produces performance issues, the custom script ID identifies where the update will need to occur.  This ID can also be used as a precaution to speed up performance fixes, if necessary.  Note:  The Script ID must be unique or the performance enhancements will affect each query with the same customScriptID. |

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - query.runSuiteQLPaged(options)
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_157960586441.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. query.runSuiteQLPaged(options)

# query.runSuiteQLPaged(options)

Important: 

You must specify a sorting order in the query definition when using this method to avoid duplicate or missing results. The query definition must provide a unique and unambiguous sorting order with a specified precedence.

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Method Description** | Runs an arbitrary SuiteQL query as a paged query.  SuiteQL is a query language based on the SQL-92 revision of the SQL database query language. It provides advanced query capabilities you can use to access your NetSuite records and data.  You can specify the SuiteQL query as one of the following:   * A string representation of the SuiteQL query     ```                           var results = query.runSuiteQLPaged({       query: 'SELECT customer.entityid, customer.email FROM customer',       pageSize: 10   });   ``` * A [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html) object     ```                           // To use this approach, you must load the N/util module in your script   // In this example, mySuiteQLCustomerQuery is an existing SuiteQL object   var pageSizeObject = {       pageSize: 10   };   var results = query.runSuiteQL(util.extend(mySuiteQLCustomerQuery, pageSizeObject));   ```     Although this approach is supported, you should create a [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html) object and call [SuiteQL.runPaged(options)](section_157960491275.html), if possible, to run a paged SuiteQL query. * A JavaScript Object that contains a `query` property and, optionally, a `params` property     ```                           var results = query.runSuiteQL({       query: 'SELECT customer.entityid, customer.email FROM customer WHERE customer.isperson = ?',       params: [true], pageSize: 10   });   ```   Important:  You cannot retrieve the columns (or column names) from the results of this method. If you need to refer to the columns used in the query, create a [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html) object, which contains the columns in the query in the [SuiteQL.columns](section_157960405619.html) property. Then, pass the object to this method, or use [SuiteQL.runPaged(options)](section_157960491275.html), to run the query.  Note:  If the SuiteAnalytics Connect feature is enabled in your NetSuite account, there is no limit to the number of results this method can return. If the SuiteAnalytics Connect feature is not enabled, this method can return a maximum of 100,000 results across all pages in the result set. For more information about SuiteAnalytics Connect, see [SuiteAnalytics Connect](chapter_3963845427.html).  For more information and examples of using SuiteQL in the N/query module, see [SuiteQL in the N/query Module](section_157960623712.html). For more information about SuiteQL in general, see [SuiteQL](section_156257770590.html). |
| **Returns** | [query.PagedData](section_1510779273.html)  Important:  This method returns a maximum of 1000 pages. |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Governance** | 10 units |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Sibling Module Members** | [N/query Module Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510352106) |
| **Since** | 2020.1 |

## Parameters

Note: 

The `options` parameter is a JavaScript object.

| Parameter | Type | Required / Optional | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `options.query` | string | required | The string representation of the SuiteQL query to run. |
| `options.params` | <string | number | > | optional | The parameters to use in the SuiteQL query. |
| `options.pageSize` | number | optional | The size of each page in the query results. The default value is 50 results per page. The minimum page size is 5 results per page, and the maximum page size is 1000 results per page. |
| `options.customScriptId` | string | optional | A unique identifier used for potential performance issues in a query.  If your query produces performance issues, the custom script ID identifies where the update will need to occur.  This ID can also be used as a precaution to speed up performance fixes, if necessary.  Note:  The Script ID must be unique or the performance enhancements will affect each query with the same customScriptID. |
| `options.metaDataProvider` | string | optional | Indicates whether the query should fail if you lack the necessary permissions for some fields or records.  If set to `SUITE_QL`:  The query fails if you attempt to access fields or records without the necessary permissions.  If set to `STATIC`:  The query succeeds even if you lack permissions for some fields or records, but it does not return any data for those fields or records.  Defaults to `SUITE_QL`. |

## Errors

| Error Code | Thrown If |
| --- | --- |
| `MISSING_REQD_ARGUMENT` | The parameter is missing. |
| `SSS_INVALID_TYPE_ARG` | Types other than string, number, or are included in the `options.params`. |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var results = query.runSuiteQLPaged({
        query: 'SELECT customer.entityid, customer.email FROM customer WHERE customer.isperson = ?',
        params: [true],
        pageSize: 20,
        customScriptId: 'myCustomScriptId'
    });
...
// Add additional code
```
