## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - query.runSuiteQLPaged.promise(options)
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_0429112941.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. query.runSuiteQLPaged.promise(options)

# query.runSuiteQLPaged.promise(options)

Important: 

You must specify a sorting order in the query definition when using this method to avoid duplicate or missing results. The query definition must provide a unique and unambiguous sorting order with a specified precedence.

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Method Description** | Asynchronously runs an arbitrary SuiteQL query as a paged query.  SuiteQL is a query language based on the SQL-92 revision of the SQL database query language. It provides advanced query capabilities you can use to access your NetSuite records and data.  You can specify the SuiteQL query as one of the following:   * A string representation of the SuiteQL query     ```                           var results = query.runSuiteQLPaged.promise({       query: 'SELECT customer.entityid, customer.email FROM customer',       pageSize: 10   });   ``` * A [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html) object     ```                           // To use this approach, you must load the N/util module in your script   // In this example, mySuiteQLCustomerQuery is an existing SuiteQL object   var pageSizeObject = {       pageSize: 10   };   var results = query.runSuiteQL(util.extend(mySuiteQLCustomerQuery, pageSizeObject));   ```     Although this approach is supported, you should create a [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html) object and call [SuiteQL.runPaged(options)](section_157960491275.html), if possible, to run a paged SuiteQL query. * A JavaScript Object that contains a `query` property and, optionally, a `params` property     ```                           var results = query.runSuiteQL({       query: 'SELECT customer.entityid, customer.email FROM customer WHERE customer.isperson = ?',       params: [true], pageSize: 10   });   ```   Important:  You cannot retrieve the columns (or column names) from the results of this method. If you need to refer to the columns used in the query, create a [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html) object, which contains the columns in the query in the [SuiteQL.columns](section_157960405619.html) property. Then, pass the object to this method, or use [SuiteQL.runPaged(options)](section_157960491275.html), to run the query.  Note:  If the SuiteAnalytics Connect feature is enabled in your NetSuite account, there is no limit to the number of results this method can return. If the SuiteAnalytics Connect feature is not enabled, this method can return a maximum of 100,000 results across all pages in the result set. For more information about SuiteAnalytics Connect, see [SuiteAnalytics Connect](chapter_3963845427.html).  For more information and examples of using SuiteQL in the N/query module, see [SuiteQL in the N/query Module](section_157960623712.html). For more information about SuiteQL in general, see [SuiteQL](section_156257770590.html). |
| **Returns** | [Promise Object](section_4387812940.html)  Important:  This method returns a maximum of 1000 pages. |
| **Synchronous Version** | [query.runSuiteQLPaged(options)](section_157960586441.html) |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Governance** | 10 units |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Sibling Module Members** | [N/query Module Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510352106) |
| **Since** | 2020.1 |

## Parameters

Note: 

The `options` parameter is a JavaScript object.

| Parameter | Type | Required / Optional | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `options.query` | string | required | The string representation of the SuiteQL query to run. |
| `options.params` | <string | number | > | optional | The parameters to use in the SuiteQL query. |
| `options.pageSize` | number | optional | The size of each page in the query results. The default value is 50 results per page. The minimum page size is 5 results per page, and the maximum page size is 1000 results per page. |
| `options.customScriptId` | string | optional | A unique identifier used for potential performance issues in a query.  If your query produces performance issues, the custom script ID identifies where the update will need to occur.  This ID can also be used as a precaution to speed up performance fixes, if necessary.  Note:  The Script ID must be unique or the performance enhancements will affect each query with the same customScriptID. |

## Errors

| Error Code | Thrown If |
| --- | --- |
| `MISSING_REQD_ARGUMENT` | The parameter is missing. |
| `SSS_INVALID_TYPE_ARG` | Types other than string, number, or are included in the `options.params`. |

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - Query.sort
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_1510781853.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. [query.Query](section_1510275177.html)
7. Query.sort

# Query.sort

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Property Description** | An array of [query.Sort](section_1510779222.html) objects used for sorting.  This object encapsulates a sort based on the [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) or [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) object. The [query.Sort](section_1510779222.html) object describes a sort that is placed on a particular query result column.  To create a sort:   * Use [Query.createSort(options)](section_1510780402.html) to create a sort based on the initial query definition created with [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html). * Use [Component.createSort(options)](section_1510785047.html) to create a sort based on a join relationship created with [Query.autoJoin(options)](section_1530819144.html) or [Component.autoJoin(options)](section_1530818573.html). * Assign all created sorts as values to [Query.sort](section_1510781853.html). For an example, see [Syntax](#subsect_1510781853). |
| **Type** | [query.Sort](section_1510779222.html)[] |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) |
| **Sibling Object Members** | [Query Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510352143) |
| **Since** | 2018.1 |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myCustomerQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.CUSTOMER
    });
    var mySalesRepJoin = myCustomerQuery.autoJoin({
        fieldId: 'salesrep'
    });
    myCustomerQuery.columns = [
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'entityid'
        }),
        mySalesRepJoin.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'firstname'
        }),
        mySalesRepJoin.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'email'
        })
    ];
    myCustomerQuery.sort = [
        myCustomerQuery.createSort({
            column: myCustomerQuery.columns[1]
        }),
        mySalesRepJoin.createSort({
            column: myCustomerQuery.columns[0],
            ascending: false
        })
    ];
...
// Add additional code
```

|  |  |

| **Object Description** | A sort based on the [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) or [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) object. The `query.Sort` object describes a sort that is placed on a particular query result column.  To create a sort:   * Use [Query.createSort(options)](section_1510780402.html) to create a sort based on the initial query definition created with [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html). * Use [Component.createSort(options)](section_1510785047.html) to create a sort based on a join relationship created with [Query.autoJoin(options)](section_1530819144.html) or [Component.autoJoin(options)](section_1530818573.html). * Assign all created sorts as values to [Query.sort](section_1510781853.html).         type: query.Type.CUSTOMER
```
    });

        fieldId: 'salesrep'
    });

        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'entityid'
        }),
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'id'
        }),

            fieldId: 'entityid'
        }),
        mySalesRepJoin.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'email'
        }),
        mySalesRepJoin.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'hiredate'
        })
    ];
    myCustomerQuery.sort = [
        myCustomerQuery.createSort({
            column: myCustomerQuery.columns[1]
        }),
        mySalesRepJoin.createSort({
            column: mySalesRepJoin.columns[0],
            ascending: false
        })
    ];
    var resultSet = myCustomerQuery.run();
...
```

# query.SortLocale

Note: 

JavaScript does not include an enumeration type. The SuiteScript 2.x documentation uses the term enumeration (or enum) to describe a plain JavaScript object with a flat, map-like structure. In this object, each key points to a read-only string value.

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Enum Description** | Holds the string values for sort locales supported with the [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html). This enum is used to pass the locale argument to [Query.createSort(options)](section_1510780402.html) and [Component.createSort(options)](section_1510785047.html). |

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - query.SuiteQL
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_157960384819.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. query.SuiteQL

# query.SuiteQL

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Object Description** | A SuiteQL query.  SuiteQL is a query language based on the SQL-92 revision of the SQL database query language. It provides advanced query capabilities you can use to access your NetSuite records and data.  Use [Query.toSuiteQL()](section_157960522744.html) to create this object. This method converts an existing [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) object to its corresponding SuiteQL representation as a `query.SuiteQL` object. You can use [SuiteQL.run()](section_157960470046.html) to run the query and obtain the results as a [query.ResultSet](section_1510779235.html) object. You can also use [SuiteQL.runPaged(options)](section_157960491275.html) to run the query as a paged query and obtain the results as a [query.PagedData](section_1510779273.html) object.  When you convert a [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) object to a `query.SuiteQL` object, the resulting SuiteQL query is the same as the original query. It includes the same query result columns, sort order, and conditions that were set on the original query. When you run the resulting SuiteQL query using [SuiteQL.run()](section_157960470046.html) or [SuiteQL.runPaged(options)](section_157960491275.html), you receive the same results as you would if you ran the original query using [Query.run(options)](section_1510780212.html) or [Query.runPaged(options)](section_1510780277.html).  For more information and examples of using SuiteQL in the N/query module, see [SuiteQL in the N/query Module](section_157960623712.html). For more information about SuiteQL in general, see [SuiteQL](section_156257770590.html). |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Methods and Properties** | [SuiteQL Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_157980851724) |
| **Since** | 2020.1 |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    // myQuery is an existing query.Query object
    var mySuiteQLQuery = myQuery.toSuiteQL();
    var results = mySuiteQLQuery.run();
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - Query.toSuiteQL()
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_157960522744.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. [query.Query](section_1510275177.html)
7. Query.toSuiteQL()

# Query.toSuiteQL()

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Method Description** | Converts this [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) object to its corresponding SuiteQL representation.  This method returns a [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html) object that represents the same query as the original [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) object. This object includes the [SuiteQL.columns](section_157960405619.html), [SuiteQL.params](section_157960427733.html), [SuiteQL.query](section_157960443690.html), and [SuiteQL.type](section_157960456167.html) properties. You can run the query using [SuiteQL.run()](section_157960470046.html), or you can run the query as a paged query using [SuiteQL.runPaged(options)](section_157960491275.html).  Important:  The resulting SuiteQL query string (contained in the [SuiteQL.query](section_157960443690.html) property) does not include any aliases you set on query result columns in the original [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) object. For more information about aliases, see [Column.alias](section_156336566313.html).  For more information and examples of using SuiteQL in the N/query module, see [SuiteQL in the N/query Module](section_157960623712.html). For more information about SuiteQL in general, see [SuiteQL](section_156257770590.html). |
| **Returns** | [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html) |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Governance** | None |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) |
| **Sibling Object Members** | [Query Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510352143) |
| **Since** | 2020.1 |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    // myQuery is an existing query.Query object
    var mySuiteQLQuery = myQuery.toSuiteQL();
    var results = mySuiteQLQuery.run();
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - Query.type

7. Query.type

# Query.type

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Property Description** | The initial query type of the query definition.  This property is set during the of [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html). |
| **Type** | string (read-only) |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) |
| **Sibling Object Members** | [Query Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510352143) |
| **Since** | 2018.1 |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myCustomerQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.CUSTOMER
    });
    var theType = myCustomerQuery.type;
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - query.Type
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_1510878994.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)

5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. query.Type

# query.Type

Note: 

JavaScript does not include an enumeration type. The SuiteScript 2.x documentation uses the term enumeration (or enum) to describe a plain JavaScript object with a flat, map-like structure. In this object, each key points to a read-only string value.

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Enum Description** | Holds the string values for query types used in the query definition. This enum is used to pass the initial query type argument to [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html).  Important:  The N/query module supports the same record types that are supported by the SuiteAnalytics Workbook interface. For more information, see [Available Record Types](section_1543418356.html). |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Sibling Module Members** | [N/query Module Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510352106) |
| **Since** | 2018.1 |

## Values

Note: 

Before using these values, consider the following:

* A query type is not the same as a record type. The supported query types listed below do not necessarily correspond with the supported record types listed in the [N/record Module](section_4267255811.html).
* Depending on your account, role, and enabled features, some of these values may not be available.
* Custom record types are not included in this enum.
* You must configure your account settings according to the query type used in your scripts to avoid potential errors.

| `ACCOUNT` | account |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
... 
    var myCustomerQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.CUSTOMER
    });
    var mySalesRepJoin = myCustomerQuery.autoJoin({
        fieldId: 'salesrep'
    });
    var firstCondition = myCustomerQuery.createCondition({
        fieldId: 'id',
        operator: query.Operator.EQUAL,
        values: 107
    });
    var secondCondition = myCustomerQuery.createCondition({
        fieldId: 'id',
        operator: query.Operator.EQUAL,
        values: 2647
    });
    var thirdCondition = mySalesRepJoin.createCondition({
        fieldId: 'email',
        operator: query.Operator.START_WITH_NOT,
        values: 'foo'
    });
    myCustomerQuery.condition = myCustomerQuery.and(thirdCondition,myCustomerQuery.or(firstCondition, secondCondition));
    var resultSet = myCustomerQuery.run();
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - Relative Dates in the N/query Module
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_1549916938.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. Relative Dates in the N/query Module

# Relative Dates in the N/query Module

You can use relative dates when you create query conditions. The [query.RelativeDate](section_1544109440.html) object represents a specific date or moment in time relative to the current date. Each of the values in the [query.RelativeDateRange](section_1544111773.html) enum represents a range of dates relative to the current date. When you use a [query.RelativeDate](section_1544109440.html) object or [query.RelativeDateRange](section_1544111773.html) enum value to create a query condition, make sure that you use an operator that makes sense for the relative date that you provide to [Query.createCondition(options)](section_1510780329.html) or [Component.createCondition(options)](section_1510784922.html). The [query.Operator](section_1510275752.html) enum contains the supported operators for the N/query module, but not all operators apply to relative dates. Use the following operators with relative dates:

* `AFTER`
* `AFTER_NOT`
* `BEFORE`
* `BEFORE_NOT`
* `ON`
* `ON_NOT`
* `ON_OR_AFTER`
* `ON_OR_AFTER_NOT`
* `ON_OR_BEFORE`
* `ON_OR_BEFORE_NOT`
* `WITHIN`
* `WITHIN_NOT`

When you create a query condition using the `WITHIN` or `WITHIN_NOT` operators and a `query.RelativeDate` object, the condition uses the current date as one of the boundaries of the date range. For example, consider the following `query.RelativeDate` object that represents a date two days before the current date:

```
          var myDatesAgo = query.createRelativeDate({
    dateId: query.DateId.DAYS_AGO,
    value: 2
});
```

You can use this `myDatesAgo` object when you create a query condition. Consider the following query condition that is created using the `WITHIN` operator and this `myDatesAgo` object:

```
          var myCondition = myQuery.createCondition({
    fieldId: 'trandate',
    operator: query.Operator.WITHIN,
    values: myDatesAgo
});
```

This query condition matches dates that are between two days ago and the current date (the day before yesterday, yesterday, and today).

Conversely, consider the following `query.RelativeDate` object that represents a date two days after the current date:

```
          var myDatesFromNow = query.createRelativeDate({
    dateId: query.DateId.DAYS_FROM_NOW,
    value: 2
});
```

If you create a query condition using the `WITHIN` operator and this `myDatesFromNow` object, the condition matches dates that are between the current date and two days from now (today, tomorrow, and the day after tomorrow).

You can use the `query.RelativeDate` object, the [query.RelativeDateRange](section_1544111773.html) enum, and the `WITHIN` operator to specify complex date ranges. You can do this in several ways:

* Use a single `query.RelativeDate` object or [query.RelativeDateRange](section_1544111773.html) enum value. When you use a single `query.RelativeDate` object, the object represents a specific moment in time, so the current date is used automatically as one of the boundaries. When you use a single `query.RelativeDateRange` enum value, the enum value represents a range of dates, so the `start` and `end` properties of the date range are used automatically as the boundaries. For example:

  ```
                var myComplexCondition = myQuery.createCondition({
      fieldId: 'trandate',
      operator: query.Operator.WITHIN,
      values: query.RelativeDateRange.SAME_DAY_LAST_WEEK
  });
  ```

  In this example, the first boundary is the beginning of the same day last week, and the second boundary is the end of the same day last week. Using `query.RelativeDateRange.SAME_DAY_LAST_WEEK` is equivalent to using either of the following:

  + `query.RelativeDateRange.SAME_DAY_LAST_WEEK.interval`
  + `[query.RelativeDateRange.SAME_DAY_LAST_WEEK.start, query.RelativeDateRange.SAME_DAY_LAST_WEEK.end]`
* Use the `start` and `end` properties of values in the [query.RelativeDateRange](section_1544111773.html) enum directly in the `values` parameter for [Query.createCondition(options)](section_1510780329.html) or [Component.createCondition(options)](section_1510784922.html). For example:

  ```
                var myComplexCondition = myQuery.createCondition({
      fieldId: 'trandate',
      operator: query.Operator.WITHIN,
      values: [query.RelativeDateRange.THIS_FISCAL_YEAR.start, query.RelativeDateRange.YESTERDAY.end]
  });
  ```
* Use a combination of [query.RelativeDateRange](section_1544111773.html) enum values and custom `query.RelativeDate` objects. For example:

  ```
                var myEndDate = query.createRelativeDate({
      dateId: query.DateId.WEEKS_AGO,
      value: 2
  });

  var myComplexCondition = myQuery.createCondition({
      fieldId: 'trandate',
      operator: query.Operator.WITHIN,
      values: [query.RelativeDateRange.THREE_FISCAL_YEARS_AGO.start, myEndDate]
  });
  ```

[General Notices](chapter_N000004.html)

# RelativeDate.dateId

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Property Description** | The date ID of the relative date.  For relative dates that you create using [query.createRelativeDate(options)](section_1544108154.html), the value of this property is set when that method is executed. For relative dates that are included in the [query.RelativeDateRange](section_1544111773.html) enum, the value of this property is always available (for example, `query.RelativeDateRange.YESTERDAY.dateId`).  This property uses values from the [query.DateId](section_1544111587.html) enum. |
| **Type** | string (read-only) |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.RelativeDate](section_1544109440.html) |
| **Sibling Object Members** | [RelativeDate Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1544530447) |
| **Since** | 2019.1 |

```
        dateId: query.DateId.WEEKS_AGO,
```

# RelativeDate.interval

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Property Description** | The interval that the relative date represents.  For relative dates that you create using [query.createRelativeDate(options)](section_1544108154.html), the value of this property is set when that method is executed. For relative date ranges that are included in the [query.RelativeDateRange](section_1544111773.html) enum, the value of this property is always available (for example, `query.RelativeDateRange.YESTERDAY.interval`).  Important:  Do not use this property explicitly in your scripts. It is available so you can see the exact date interval that is used with the `query.Operator.WITHIN` and `query.Operator.WITHIN_NOT` operators in query conditions. |
| **Type** | Object (read-only) |

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - RelativeDate.isRange
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_1552334952.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. [query.RelativeDate](section_1544109440.html)
7. RelativeDate.isRange

# RelativeDate.isRange

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Property Description** | Whether the relative date represents a range of dates or a specific moment in time.  For relative date ranges that you obtain from the [query.RelativeDateRange](section_1544111773.html) enum, the value of this property is `true` (the relative date represents a range of dates). For all other relative dates (such as those that you create using [query.createRelativeDate(options)](section_1544108154.html)), the value of this property is `false` (the relative date represents a specific moment in time). |
| **Type** | boolean (read-only) |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.RelativeDate](section_1544109440.html) |
| **Sibling Object Members** | [RelativeDate Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1544530447) |
| **Since** | 2019.1 |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myRelativeDate = query.createRelativeDate({
        dateId: query.DateId.WEEKS_AGO,
        value: 2
    });

    var isARange = myRelativeDate.isRange; // isARange is false
    var isAnotherRange = query.RelativeDateRange.LAST_MONTH_ONE_FISCAL_YEAR_AGO.isRange; // isAnotherRange is true
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - Result.asMap()
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_156336629343.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. [query.Result](section_1510779258.html)
7. Result.asMap()

# Result.asMap()

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Method Description** | Returns the query result as a mapped result. A mapped result is a JavaScript object with key-value pairs. In this object, the key is either the field ID or the alias that was used for the corresponding [query.Column](section_1510779196.html) object. |
| **Returns** | Object |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Governance** | None |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.Result](section_1510779258.html) |
| **Sibling Object Members** | [Result Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510858930) |
| **Since** | 2019.2 |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myCustomerQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.CUSTOMER
    });
    var mySalesRepJoin = myCustomerQuery.autoJoin({
        fieldId: 'salesrep'
    });
    myCustomerQuery.columns = [
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'entityid',
            alias: 'cust'
        }),
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'id'
        }),
        mySalesRepJoin.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'entityid'
        }),
        mySalesRepJoin.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'email'
        }), mySalesRepJoin.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'hiredate'
        })
    ];
    var resultSet = myCustomerQuery.run();
    for (var i = 0; i < resultSet.results.length; i++) {
        var mResult = resultSet.results[i].asMap();
        log.debug(mResult);
    }
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - Result.getValue(options)
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/article_0522071257.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. [query.Result](section_1510779258.html)
7. Result.getValue(options)

# Result.getValue(options)

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Method Description** | Gets the value at a given index in [Result.values](section_1510859061.html). Value types correspond to the [ResultSet.types](section_1510857678.html) property. Values correspond to the values for [ResultSet.columns](section_1510857693.html). |
| **Returns** | <string | number | Date | null> (read-only) |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Governance** | None |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.Result](section_1510779258.html) |
| **Sibling Object Members** | [Result Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510858930) |
| **Since** | 2018.2 |

## Parameters

| Parameter | Type | Required / Optional | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `options` | number | required | The index of the element from [Result.values](section_1510859061.html) that you want the method to return. |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
const COLUMNS = ['entityid', 'id'];
const employeeInfo = {};

let employeeQuery = query.create({
  type: query.Type.EMPLOYEE
});
COLUMNS.forEach(column => {
  employeeQuery.columns.push(employeeQuery.createColumn({
    fieldId: column
  }));
});

const resultSet = employeeQuery.run();
const results = resultSet.results || [];

results.forEach(result => {
  for (let i = 0; i < result.values.length; i++) {
    employeeInfo[COLUMNS[i]] = result.getValue(i);
  }
});
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - ResultSet.asMappedResults()

# ResultSet.asMappedResults()

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Method Description** | Returns the query result set as an array of mapped results. A mapped result is a JavaScript object with key-value pairs. In this object, the key is either the field ID or the alias that was used for the corresponding [query.Column](section_1510779196.html) object. When you call this method, [Result.asMap()](section_156336629343.html) is called on each [query.Result](section_1510779258.html) object in the result set. |
| **Returns** | Object[] |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Governance** | None |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.ResultSet](section_1510779235.html) |
| **Sibling Object Members** | [ResultSet Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510790719) |
| **Since** | 2019.2 |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myCustomerQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.CUSTOMER
    });
    var mySalesRepJoin = myCustomerQuery.autoJoin({
        fieldId: 'salesrep'
    });
    myCustomerQuery.columns = [
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'entityid',
            alias: 'cust'
        }),
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'id'
        }),
        mySalesRepJoin.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'entityid' 
        }),
        mySalesRepJoin.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'email'
        }),
        mySalesRepJoin.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'hiredate'
        })
    ];
    var resultSet = myCustomerQuery.run();
    var mrSet = resultSet.asMappedResults();
...
// Add additional code
```

|  |  |

| **Property Description** | An array of query return column references. The `ResultSet.columns` values correspond with the [ResultSet.types](section_1510857678.html) values. |
| **Type** | [query.Column](section_1510779196.html)[] (read-only) |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.ResultSet](section_1510779235.html) |

| **Since** | 2018.1 |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myCustomerQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.CUSTOMER
    });
    myCustomerQuery.columns = [
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'entityid'
        }),
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'email'
        })
    ];
    var queryResultSet = myCustomerQuery.run();
    var theColumns = queryResultSet.columns;
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - ResultSet.iterator()

# ResultSet.iterator()

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Method Description** | Standard SuiteScript 2.0 object for iterating through results |
| **Returns** | [Iterator](section_0831085754.html) object |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Governance** | None |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.ResultSet](section_1510779235.html) |
| **Sibling Object Members** | [ResultSet Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510790719) |
| **Since** | 2018.1 |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myCustomerQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.CUSTOMER
    });
    myCustomerQuery.columns = [
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'entityid'
        }),
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'firstname'
        }),
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'email'
        })
    ];
    var queryResultSet = myCustomerQuery.run(); // Fetch results using an iterator
    var iterator = queryResultSet.iterator();
    iterator.each(function(result) {
        var currentResult = result.value;
        log.debug(currentResult);
        return true;
    });
    
    // Alternatively, fetch results using a loop
    var queryResults = queryResultSet.results;
    for (var i = 0; i < queryResults.length; i++) {
        var currentResult = queryResults[i]; log.debug(currentResult);
    }
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - Scripting with the N/query Module
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_1532440865.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. Scripting with the N/query Module

# Scripting with the N/query Module

The N/query module lets you create and run queries using the SuiteAnalytics Workbook query engine. Before you start creating your queries, you should be familiar with the module objects and how to use them, as well as some of the terminology used in the N/query module. You can also take a look at a script walkthrough that explains how to create queries using different approaches.

* [N/query Module Objects](#subsect_1527642761)
* [N/query Module Terminology](#subsect_1519851639)

## N/query Module Objects

The N/query module includes the following objects:

* [Query and Component Objects](#subsect_1527642796)
* [Condition Object](#subsect_1527642813)
* [RelativeDate Object](#subsect_1549905133)
* [Column Object](#subsect_1527642835)
* [Sort Object](#subsect_1527642857)
* [ResultSet and Result Objects](#subsect_1527642999)
* [Page, PagedData, and PageRange Objects](#subsect_1527642880)

### Query and Component Objects

The [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) object and the [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) object are the primary building blocks for a query created with the N/query module. Each query creates one [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) object and one or more [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) objects. The [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) object encapsulates the query definition, and the [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) object encapsulates one component of the query definition.

To create a query with the N/query module:

1. Use the [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html) method to create your initial query definition (the [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) object). The initial query definition uses one search type. For available search types, see [query.Type](section_1510878994.html).
2. After you create the initial query definition, use [Query.autoJoin(options)](section_1530819144.html), [Query.joinFrom(options)](section_1530819218.html), or [Query.joinTo(options)](section_1530819329.html) to create your first join.
3. Use any of the following methods to create subsequent joins:

   * [Query.autoJoin(options)](section_1530819144.html)
   * [Query.joinFrom(options)](section_1530819218.html)
   * [Query.joinTo(options)](section_1530819329.html)
   * [Component.autoJoin(options)](section_1530818573.html)
   * [Component.joinFrom(options)](section_1530818705.html)
   * [Component.joinTo(options)](section_1530818855.html)

The query definition always contains at least one [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) object. Each new component is created as a child of the previous component, and all components exist as children of the query definition. You can think of a component as a building block; each new component builds on the previous component created. The last component created encapsulates the relationship between it and all of its parent components.

Queries with joins contain multiple components. The query definition contains a child [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) object for each of the following:

* **The initial query definition:** The initial [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) object is called the root component. It encapsulates the initial search type passed to [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html). The root component is automatically created with the initial query definition and is a child to the [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) object. The [Query.root](section_1510781874.html) property contains a reference to the root component.
* **The first join:** The second [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) object is created with [Query.autoJoin(options)](section_1530819144.html), [Query.joinFrom(options)](section_1530819218.html), or [Query.joinTo(options)](section_1530819329.html). It encapsulates the relationship between the initial query definition and the second search type. This relationship is determined by the join ID passed to these methods, as well as whether [Query.joinFrom(options)](section_1530819218.html) or [Query.joinTo(options)](section_1530819329.html) was used to create an explicit directional join. The second [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) object is a child to the root component.
* **Each subsequent join:** The third [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) object is created with [Component.autoJoin(options)](section_1530818573.html), [Component.joinFrom(options)](section_1530818705.html), or [Component.joinTo(options)](section_1530818855.html). All subsequent joins are also created using these methods. Each of these [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) objects encapsulates the relationship between all previous search types and the new search type. This relationship is determined by the join ID passed to these methods, as well as whether [Component.joinFrom(options)](section_1530818705.html) or [Component.joinTo(options)](section_1530818855.html) was used to create an explicit directional join.

### Condition Object

A condition narrows the query results. The [query.Condition](section_1510779210.html) object performs the same function as the [search.Filter](section_4345767603.html) object in the [N/search Module](section_4345764122.html). The primary difference is that [query.Condition](section_1510779210.html) objects can contain other [query.Condition](section_1510779210.html) objects.

To create conditions:

* Use [Query.createCondition(options)](section_1510780329.html) to create conditions for the initial query definition created with [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html).
* Use [Component.createCondition(options)](section_1510784922.html) to create conditions for the join relationships created with [Query.autoJoin(options)](section_1530819144.html), [Query.joinFrom(options)](section_1530819218.html)/[Query.joinTo(options)](section_1530819329.html), [Component.autoJoin(options)](section_1530818573.html), or [Component.joinFrom(options)](section_1530818705.html)/[Component.joinTo(options)](section_1530818855.html).
* If you have multiple conditions, use [Query.and(conditions)](section_1510780422.html), [Query.or(conditions)](section_1510780444.html), and [Query.not(condition)](section_1510780462.html) to create a new nested condition.
* If you want to use a formula to define your conditions, assign the formula to [Condition.formula](section_1510789560.html).
* Assign your simple or nested conditions as array values to [Query.condition](section_1510781832.html).

### RelativeDate Object

The [query.RelativeDate](section_1544109440.html) object represents a date that is relative to the current date. You can use relative dates when you create query conditions.

To create relative dates:

* Use [query.createRelativeDate(options)](section_1544108154.html) to create a [query.RelativeDate](section_1544109440.html) object. When you call [query.createRelativeDate(options)](section_1544108154.html), use the values in the [query.DateId](section_1544111587.html) enum to specify a date that is relative to the current date.
* Use [Query.createCondition(options)](section_1510780329.html) or [Component.createCondition(options)](section_1510784922.html) to create a condition using the [query.RelativeDate](section_1544109440.html) object. Alternatively, you can create a condition using values in the [query.RelativeDateRange](section_1544111773.html) enum.
* If you have multiple conditions, use [Query.and(conditions)](section_1510780422.html), [Query.or(conditions)](section_1510780444.html), and [Query.not(condition)](section_1510780462.html) to create a new nested condition.
* Assign your simple or nested conditions as array values to [Query.condition](section_1510781832.html).

### Column Object

The [query.Column](section_1510779196.html) object is the equivalent of the [search.Column](section_4345767216.html) object in the [N/search Module](section_4345764122.html). The [query.Column](section_1510779196.html) object describes the field types (columns) that are displayed from the query results.

To create columns:

* Use [Query.createColumn(options)](section_1510780373.html) to create a column on the initial query definition created with [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html).
* Use [Component.createColumn(options)](section_1510784945.html) to create a column on a join relationship created with [Query.autoJoin(options)](section_1530819144.html), [Query.joinFrom(options)](section_1530819218.html)/[Query.joinTo(options)](section_1530819329.html), [Component.autoJoin(options)](section_1530818573.html), or [Component.joinFrom(options)](section_1530818705.html)/[Component.joinTo(options)](section_1530818855.html).
* If you want to use a formula to define your columns, assign the formula to [Column.formula](section_1510789062.html).
* Assign all created columns as array values to [Query.columns](section_1510781812.html).

### Sort Object

The [query.Sort](section_1510779222.html) object describes how query results are sorted (for example, ascending or descending, case sensitive or case insensitive, and so on).

To create a sort:

* Use [Query.createSort(options)](section_1510780402.html) to create a sort on the initial query definition created with [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html).
* Use [Component.createSort(options)](section_1510785047.html) to create a sort based on a join relationship created with [Query.autoJoin(options)](section_1530819144.html), [Query.joinFrom(options)](section_1530819218.html)/[Query.joinTo(options)](section_1530819329.html), [Component.autoJoin(options)](section_1530818573.html), or [Component.joinFrom(options)](section_1530818705.html)/[Component.joinTo(options)](section_1530818855.html).
* Assign all created sorts as array values to [Query.sort](section_1510781853.html).

### ResultSet and Result Objects

When you are ready to execute your query, call [Query.run(options)](section_1510780212.html). This method returns a [query.ResultSet](section_1510779235.html) object, which encapsulates the metadata for the set of results returned by the query.

To access your query results, iterate through the [ResultSet.results](section_1510857646.html) array. Each member of the [ResultSet.results](section_1510857646.html) array is a [query.Result](section_1510779258.html) object. The [query.Result](section_1510779258.html) object encapsulates a single row of the result set.

### Page, PagedData, and PageRange Objects

You also can execute your query by calling [Query.runPaged(options)](section_1510780277.html). This method returns a [query.PagedData](section_1510779273.html) object, which encapsulates a set of paged query results.

To access your query results, iterate through the paged query results using [PagedData.iterator()](section_1510861317.html). You can access each page of the query results, which are represented by [query.Page](section_1510779287.html) objects. The [query.PageRange](section_1510779296.html) object encapsulates the range of query results for a page.

## N/query Module Terminology

| Term | Definition | For More Information |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Aggregate function | An aggregate function performs a calculation on a column of values and returns a single value. You can add aggregate functions to conditions and query results columns. | * [query.Aggregate](section_1510878932.html) * [Component.createColumn(options)](section_1510784945.html) * [Component.createCondition(options)](section_1510784922.html) * [Query.createColumn(options)](section_1510780373.html) * [Query.createCondition(options)](section_1510780329.html) |
| Column | A column describes the field types (columns) that are displayed from the query results. A column is also known as a query results column. | * [query.Column](section_1510779196.html) |
| Component | When you script queries with the N/query module, your query is made up of one or more components, which are represented as [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) objects. You can think of a component as a building block; each new component builds on the previous component created.   * The first component created represents the initial search type and is a child of [query.Query](section_1510275177.html). * Each subsequent component created is a child of the previous component. * The last component created encapsulates the join relationship between it and all of its parent components.   A query always contains at least one component: the root component. When you create the initial query definition using [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html), the root component is created automatically. Queries with joins contain multiple components. A new component is created each time you create a join using one of the following methods:   * [Query.autoJoin(options)](section_1530819144.html), [Query.joinFrom(options)](section_1530819218.html), or [Query.joinTo(options)](section_1530819329.html) * [Component.autoJoin(options)](section_1530818573.html), [Component.joinFrom(options)](section_1530818705.html), or [Component.joinTo(options)](section_1530818855.html) | * [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) |
| Condition | A condition narrows the query results. | * [query.Condition](section_1510779210.html) |
| Formula | Formulas can be used to create conditions and columns. | * [Formulas in Searches](article_5143710889.html) * [SQL Expressions](section_N2833020.html) |
| Group | You can summarize your query results into unique groups of column values. | * [Column.groupBy](section_1510789147.html) |
| Join | A join lets you create a query based on a field type that is shared between two record types. You can use [Query.autoJoin(options)](section_1530819144.html) and [Component.autoJoin(options)](section_1530818573.html) to create a join relationship automatically based on a field that you specify. You can use [Query.joinFrom(options)](section_1530819218.html)/[Query.joinTo(options)](section_1530819329.html) and [Component.joinFrom(options)](section_1530818705.html)/[Component.joinTo(options)](section_1530818855.html) to create explicit directional join relationships from one component to another. | * [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) * [query.Component](section_1510779141.html) |
| Page | A page represents one page from a set of paged query results. When you create a query with the N/query module, you can return the results as one result set or a set of paged results. | * [Query.runPaged(options)](section_1510780277.html) * [query.PagedData](section_1510779273.html) * [query.PageRange](section_1510779296.html) * [query.Page](section_1510779287.html) |
| Paged data | Paged data represents a set of paged query results. | * [Query.runPaged(options)](section_1510780277.html) * [query.PagedData](section_1510779273.html) * [query.PageRange](section_1510779296.html) * [query.Page](section_1510779287.html) |
| Page range | A page range is a set of pages from a set of paged query results. | * [Query.runPaged(options)](section_1510780277.html) * [query.PagedData](section_1510779273.html) * [query.PageRange](section_1510779296.html) * [query.Page](section_1510779287.html) |
| Relative date | A relative date is a date that is relative to the current date. You can use relative dates when you create query conditions. | * [query.RelativeDate](section_1544109440.html) * [query.createRelativeDate(options)](section_1544108154.html) * [query.RelativeDateRange](section_1544111773.html) |
| Result | A result is a single row from a result set. | * [Query.run(options)](section_1510780212.html) * [query.ResultSet](section_1510779235.html) * [query.Result](section_1510779258.html) |
| Result set | A result set is a set of query results. | * [Query.run(options)](section_1510780212.html) * [query.ResultSet](section_1510779235.html) * [query.Result](section_1510779258.html) |
| Query definition | The query definition is the initial search type you define, plus any subsequent joins you define. The initial query definition is created with [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html). | * [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) |
| Query type | The query type is the initial query type of your query definition. It represents the record type you want to query for. It is set with the [query.Type](section_1510878994.html) enum during the execution of [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html). For example, if you want to query for customer records, specify `query.Type.CUSTOMER` as the query type when you call [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html). | * [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) * [query.Type](section_1510878994.html) |
| Sort | A sort is placed on a query results column to describe how the query results are sorted (for example, ascending or descending, case sensitive or case insensitive, and so on). | * [query.Sort](section_1510779222.html) * [Query.createSort(options)](section_1510780402.html) * [Component.createSort(options)](section_1510785047.html) |

[General Notices](chapter_N000004.html)

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - Sort.ascending
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_1530897548.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. [query.Sort](section_1510779222.html)
7. Sort.ascending

# Sort.ascending

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Property Description** | Whether the sort direction is ascending.  This property is set during the of [Query.createSort(options)](section_1510780402.html) and [Component.createSort(options)](section_1510785047.html).  The default value of this property is `true`, meaning that the sort direction is ascending. If you want the sort direction to be descending, set this property to `false`. |
| **Type** | boolean |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.Sort](section_1510779222.html) |
| **Sibling Object Members** | [Sort Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510790337) |
| **Since** | 2018.2 |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myCustomerQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.CUSTOMER
    });
    myCustomerQuery.columns = [
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'entityid'
        })
    ];
    myCustomerQuery.sort = [
        myCustomerQuery.createSort({
            column: myCustomerQuery.columns[0],
            ascending: false,
            caseSensitive: true,
            locale: query.SortLocale.EN_CA,
            nullsLast: false
        })
    ];
    var theAscending = myCustomerQuery.sort[0].ascending;
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - Sort.caseSensitive
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_1530819572.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. [query.Sort](section_1510779222.html)
7. Sort.caseSensitive

# Sort.caseSensitive

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Property Description** | Whether the sort is case sensitive.  This property is set during the of [Query.createSort(options)](section_1510780402.html) and [Component.createSort(options)](section_1510785047.html).  If a sort is case sensitive (and the sort direction is ascending), rows with column values that start with uppercase letters are listed before rows with column values that start with lowercase letters. If a sort is not case sensitive, uppercase and lowercase letters are treated the same. For example, the following list of items is sorted using a case-sensitive sort with a sort direction of ascending:   * Banana * Orange * apple * grapefruit * kiwi   Here is the same list of items sorted using a regular (not case-sensitive) sort with a sort direction of ascending:   * apple * Banana * grapefruit * kiwi * Orange   The default value of this property is `false`. |
| **Type** | boolean |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.Sort](section_1510779222.html) |
| **Sibling Object Members** | [Sort Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_1510790337) |
| **Since** | 2018.2 |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    var myCustomerQuery = query.create({
        type: query.Type.CUSTOMER
    });
    myCustomerQuery.columns = [
        myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
            fieldId: 'entityid'
        })
    ];
    myCustomerQuery.sort = [
        myCustomerQuery.createSort({
            column: myCustomerQuery.columns[0],
            ascending: false,
            caseSensitive: true,
            locale: query.SortLocale.EN_CA,
            nullsLast: false
        })
    ];
    var theCaseSensitive = myCustomerQuery.sort[0].caseSensitive;
...
// Add additional code
```

A locale represents a combination of language and region, and it can affect how certain values (such as strings) are sorted. ## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - SuiteAnalytics Workbook Overview
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/chapter_1503949328.html

1. [SuiteAnalytics](set_N576235.html)
2. [Workbook](book_1527274324.html)
3. SuiteAnalytics Workbook Overview

# SuiteAnalytics Workbook Overview

SuiteAnalytics Workbook is an analytics tool in NetSuite. With it, you can create custom workbooks that combine datasets, tables, pivot tables, and charts all in one place using the new analytics data source. The analytics data source ensures that fields show up the same way and give consistent results across all workbook visualizations. Workbook now supports multilevel joins, so you can use data from multiple record types, including custom records, when creating workbooks and datasets. Custom formula fields are also supported, letting you add fields with dynamic values to your workbooks. And you can link datasets in Workbook, so you can compare metrics from different datasets in a single workbook visualization.

The SuiteAnalytics Workbook user interface is designed so even users without much record schema or query language knowledge can create complex workbooks and datasets with simple actions like drag-and-drop. When you create a workbook or visualization, you can base it on any dataset you have access to in your account. You can also link multiple datasets to the same workbook, so you can analyze different metrics without switching tabs or workbooks. When you've connected multiple datasets to a workbook, you can link them to analyze their metrics in a pivot table or chart.

Note: 

You can't edit how datasets are linked using the Workbook interface right now, but you can use linked datasets to make new workbook visualizations. For more information, see [Dataset Linking in SuiteAnalytics Workbook](article_162627392718.html).

The Workbook user interface is great for ad hoc analysis, with instant formula validation, quick data refresh, and drill-down through your query results. The interface also has a range of customization options for advanced formatting, filtering, and visualizing your data.

The latest version of SuiteAnalytics Workbook lets you create workbooks and datasets for lots of record types. You can also use analytical record types made specifically for Workbook, like the sales (invoiced) record type.

Important: 

SuiteAnalytics Workbook isn't supported by SuiteBundler. To avoid installation errors, don't include SuiteAnalytics Workbook objects in your bundles. For more information about SuiteBundler, see [SuiteBundler Overview](chapter_N3363483.html).

To help familiarize yourself with SuiteAnalytics Workbook and better understand the content available in the Workbook Help Center, see [Getting Started with SuiteAnalytics Workbook](section_158874665729.html).

### Related Topics

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - SuiteQL in the N/query Module
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_157960623712.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. SuiteQL in the N/query Module

# SuiteQL in the N/query Module

SuiteQL is a query language based on the SQL-92 revision of the SQL database query language. It provides advanced query capabilities you can use to access your NetSuite records and data. For more information about SuiteQL, including limitations, exceptions, and more usage examples, see [SuiteQL](section_156257770590.html).

In SuiteScript, you can create and run SuiteQL queries using the N/query module. Queries created using SuiteQL can be more powerful and flexible than queries created using other APIs in the N/query module. SuiteQL queries can also provide the best query performance for many use cases. You can create your own SuiteQL query strings, which lets you create and run complex SQL queries that cannot be created otherwise. For examples of SuiteQL queries you can create, see [Examples of Using SuiteQL in the N/query Module](section_158039627694.html).

Important: 

To create your own SuiteQL query strings, you must know the names of the record types and fields you want to use. For more information about finding record type and field names, see [Finding Record Type and Field Names](section_156475462055.html).

Using the N/query module, you can run SuiteQL queries in the following ways:

* Convert an existing query (as a [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) object) to its SuiteQL representation (as a [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html) object) and run the query. To learn more, see [Converting an Existing Query to SuiteQL](#subsect_158038956754).
* Run an arbitrary SuiteQL query as a paged or non-paged query. To learn more, see [Running an Arbitrary SuiteQL Query](#subsect_158038957562).

## Converting an Existing Query to SuiteQL

If you already have a [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) object in your script (one that you created using [query.create(options)](section_1510275581.html) or loaded using [query.load(options)](section_1510349101.html)), you can convert the query to its SuiteQL representation. The [Query.toSuiteQL()](section_157960522744.html) method converts a [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) object to a [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html) object. The resulting [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html) object represents the same query as the original [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) object and, when run, returns the same query results.

Important: 

The resulting SuiteQL query string (contained in the [SuiteQL.query](section_157960443690.html) property) does not include any aliases you set on query result columns in the original [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) object. For more information about aliases, see [Column.alias](section_156336566313.html).

A [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html) object includes the following properties:

* [SuiteQL.columns](section_157960405619.html) - The result columns to be returned from the query. This property is an array of [query.Column](section_1510779196.html) objects. The value of this property is the same as the value of the [Query.columns](section_1510781812.html) property in the original [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) object.
* [SuiteQL.params](section_157960427733.html) - The parameters for the query. In SuiteQL, query conditions are represented using the `WHERE` clause and a set of parameters.
* [SuiteQL.query](section_157960443690.html) - The string representation of the SuiteQL query. This string can contain SQL clauses, record or table names, field names, operators, and more.
* [SuiteQL.type](section_157960456167.html) - The type of the query. This property uses values from the [query.Type](section_1510878994.html) enum. The value of this property is the same as the value of the [Query.type](section_1510275511.html) property in the original [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) object.

To run the SuiteQL query, use one of the following methods:

* Use [SuiteQL.run()](section_157960470046.html) to run the query as a non-paged query. This method returns the results as a [query.ResultSet](section_1510779235.html) object.
* Use [SuiteQL.runPaged(options)](section_157960491275.html) to run the query as a paged query. This method returns the results as a [query.PagedData](section_1510779273.html) object. The default page size is 50 results per page. The minimum page size is 5 results per page, and the maximum page size is 1000 results per page.

The following example shows you how to create a query as a [query.Query](section_1510275177.html) object, convert the query to SuiteQL, and run the resulting SuiteQL query as a non-paged query:

```
            var myCustomerQuery = query.create({
    type: query.Type.CUSTOMER
});

myCustomerQuery.columns = [
    myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
        fieldId: 'entityid'
    }),
    myCustomerQuery.createColumn({
        fieldId: 'email'
    })
];

myCustomerQuery.condition = myCustomerQuery.createCondition({
    fieldId: 'isperson',
    operator: query.Operator.IS,
    values: [true]
});

var mySQLCustomerQuery = myCustomerQuery.toSuiteQL();

var results = mySQLCustomerQuery.run();
```

In the preceding example, the `mySQLCustomerQuery` variable contains the resulting [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html) object after the conversion. In this object, the [SuiteQL.query](section_157960443690.html) property contains the string representation of the original query. In this example, this property contains the following string:

```
            SELECT customer.entityid AS entityidRAW /*{entityid#RAW}*/, customer.email AS emailRAW /*{email#RAW}*/ FROM customer WHERE customer.isperson = ?
```

The [SuiteQL.params](section_157960427733.html) property contains the parameter value `true`. When the SuiteQL query runs, the question mark (`?`) in the query string is replaced with the parameter value (`true`).

## Running an Arbitrary SuiteQL Query

You can create your own SuiteQL queries and run them. The [query.runSuiteQL(options)](section_157960542026.html) method lets you run an arbitrary SuiteQL query, and it returns query results as a [query.ResultSet](section_1510779235.html) object. The [query.runSuiteQLPaged(options)](section_157960586441.html) method lets you run a SuiteQL query as a paged query, and it returns query results as a [query.PagedData](section_1510779273.html) object.

To specify the SuiteQL query to run, you can provide one of the following to [query.runSuiteQL(options)](section_157960542026.html) or [query.runSuiteQLPaged(options)](section_157960586441.html):

* A string representation of the SuiteQL query

  ```
                  var results = query.runSuiteQL({
      query: 'SELECT customer.entityid, customer.email FROM customer'
  });
  ```
* A [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html) object

  ```
                  // In this example, mySuiteQLCustomerQuery is an existing SuiteQL object
  var results = query.runSuiteQL(mySuiteQLCustomerQuery);
  ```
* A JavaScript Object that contains a `query` property and, optionally, a `params` property:

  ```
                  var results = query.runSuiteQL({
      query: 'SELECT customer.entityid, customer.email FROM customer WHERE customer.isperson = ?',
      params: [true]
  });
  ```

[General Notices](chapter_N000004.html)

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - SuiteQL.params
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_157960427733.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html)
7. SuiteQL.params

# SuiteQL.params

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Property Description** | The parameters for the query.  In SuiteQL, query conditions are represented using the `WHERE` clause and a set of parameters. In a SuiteQL string, parameter values for conditions are represented using question marks (?), and the `params` property includes a list of the parameter values to use when the query runs. If the query uses more than one parameter, the order of the values in the `params` property matches the order the parameters appear in the query string.  For example, consider the following [query.Condition](section_1510779210.html) object in a query for customer records:   ```                     myQueryObject.createCondition({     fieldId: 'creditlimit',     operator: query.Operator.LESS_OR_EQUAL,     values: [50000] }); ```   If you use [Query.toSuiteQL()](section_157960522744.html) to convert this query to SuiteQL, the resulting SuiteQL query string includes the following `WHERE` clause:   ```                     WHERE customer.creditlimit <= ? ```   In the resulting [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html) object, the `params` property includes the value `50000`. |
| **Type** | <string | number | > (read-only) |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html) |
| **Sibling Object Members** | [SuiteQL Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_157980851724) |
| **Since** | 2020.1 |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    // myQuery is an existing query.Query object
    var mySuiteQLQuery = myQuery.toSuiteQL();
    var theParams = mySuiteQLQuery.params;
...
// Add additional code
```

[General Notices](chapter_N000004.html)

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - SuiteQL.query
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_157960443690.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html)
7. SuiteQL.query

# SuiteQL.query

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Property Description** | The string representation of the SuiteQL query.  This string can contain the following types of elements:   * SQL clauses, such as `SELECT`, `FROM`, and `WHERE` * Record or table names, such as `customer` * Field names using dot notation, such as `customer.entityid` * Operators for conditions, such as `=` and `>=` * Formatting characters, such as newline characters (`\n`)   This string can also contain field formatting metadata, such as `/*{entityid#RAW}*/`. When you use [Query.toSuiteQL()](section_157960522744.html) to convert a constructed query to its SuiteQL query equivalent, metadata may be added to the query string to indicate the formatting (or context) of fields in the query. For example, `/*{entityid#RAW}*/` metadata indicates that the `entityid` field is formatted using the `query.FieldContext.RAW` field context from the [query.FieldContext](section_1552071599.html) enum. This metadata is added as comments (using `/*` and `*/`) and does not affect query or the query results. |
| **Type** | string (read-only) |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html) |
| **Sibling Object Members** | [SuiteQL Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_157980851724) |
| **Since** | 2020.1 |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    // myQuery is an existing query.Query object
    var mySuiteQLQuery = myQuery.toSuiteQL();
    var theQuery = mySuiteQLQuery.query;
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - SuiteQL.run()
Source: https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/saas/netsuite/ns-online-help/section_157960470046.html

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
2. [SuiteScript](set_1502135122.html)
3. [SuiteScript 2.x API Reference](article_4140956840.html)
4. [SuiteScript 2.x Modules](chapter_4220488571.html)
5. [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html)
6. [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html)
7. SuiteQL.run()

# SuiteQL.run()

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Method Description** | Runs the SuiteQL query and returns the query results.  You can use this method to run the SuiteQL query and obtain the results as a [query.ResultSet](section_1510779235.html) object. If you want to run the SuiteQL query as a paged query, use [SuiteQL.runPaged(options)](section_157960491275.html).  Calling this method is equivalent to calling [query.runSuiteQL(options)](section_157960542026.html) and passing the [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html) object as a parameter:   ```                     // These two query calls return the same result set var firstResultSet = mySuiteQLObject.run(); var secondResultSet = query.runSuiteQL(mySuiteQLObject); ```   Note:  If the SuiteAnalytics Connect feature is enabled in your NetSuite account, there is no limit to the number of results this method can return. If the SuiteAnalytics Connect feature is not enabled, this method can return a maximum of 100,000 results. For more information about SuiteAnalytics Connect, see [SuiteAnalytics Connect](chapter_3963845427.html).  For more information and examples of using SuiteQL in the N/query module, see [SuiteQL in the N/query Module](section_157960623712.html). For more information about SuiteQL in general, see [SuiteQL](section_156257770590.html). |
| **Returns** | [query.ResultSet](section_1510779235.html) |
| **Supported Script Types** | Client and server scripts  For more information, see [SuiteScript 2.x Script Types](chapter_4387172495.html). |
| **Governance** | 10 units |
| **Module** | [N/query Module](section_1510275060.html) |
| **Parent Object** | [query.SuiteQL](section_157960384819.html) |
| **Sibling Object Members** | [SuiteQL Object Members](section_1510275060.html#subsect_157980851724) |
| **Since** | 2020.1 |

## Parameters

Note: 

The `options` parameter is a JavaScript object.

| Parameter | Type | Required / Optional | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `options.customScriptId` | string | optional | A unique identifier used for potential performance issues in a query.  If your query produces performance issues, the custom script ID identifies where the update will need to occur.  This ID can also be used as a precaution to speed up performance fixes, if necessary.  Note:  The Script ID must be unique or the performance enhancements will affect each query with the same customScriptID. |

## Syntax

Important: 

The following code sample shows the syntax for this member. It is not a functional example. For a complete script example, see [N/query Module Script Samples](section_0304035624.html).

```
            // Add additional code
...
    // myQuery is an existing query.Query object
    var mySuiteQLQuery = myQuery.toSuiteQL();
    var results = mySuiteQLQuery.run({
        customScriptId: 'myCustomScriptId'
    });
...
// Add additional code
```

## query_module: NetSuite Applications Suite - SuiteQL.runPaged(options)

1. [SuiteCloud Platform](set_N2807372.html)
